Editor's note— Res. of 5-14-96, §§ 1-01—1-20, adopted May 14, 1997, did not specifically amend the Code and has been included herein as superceding the provisions of former ch. 2, art. II relative to the board of commissioners. 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 50-14-1. 
Related laws reference— Board of commissioners, art. I. 

Sec. 2-26. - Open meetings. 
All meetings of the board of commissioners shall be held in accordance with the provisions of 50-14-1 et seq. of the Official Code of Georgia Annotated. The public shall at all times be afforded access to all meetings other than executive sessions. 
(Res. of 5-14-96, § 1-01) 
Sec. 2-27. - Regular meetings. 
Regular meetings of the board of commissioners shall be held at 6:00 p.m. on the second Tuesday of each month. All regular meetings shall be held in the Commissioner Chambers located at 213 Person Street or in such larger room as the chairman may determine. A notice containing the foregoing information shall be posted and maintained in a conspicuous place available to the general public at the regular meeting place of the board. 
(Res. of 5-14-96, § 1-14) 
Sec. 2-28. - Called meetings and rescheduled regular meetings. 
Called meetings may be scheduled by the chairman or at the request of two commissioners. Whenever a rescheduled regular meeting or any other called meeting is to be held at a time or place other than the regularly scheduled time or place, written notice of the change shall be posted for at least 24 hours at the place of the regular meetings. In addition, written or oral notice shall be given by the clerk at least 24 hours in advance of the meeting to either the legal organ of the county or a newspaper having a general circulation at least equal to that of the legal organ, and to each member of the county governing authority. 
(Res. of 5-14-96, § 1-15) 
Sec. 2-29. - Emergency meetings. 
When emergency circumstances occur, the board may hold a meeting with less than 24-hours' notice to the public. When such meetings are to be held, the clerk shall provide notice to the legal organ of the county or a newspaper with a general circulation at least equal to that of the legal organ and to each member of the county governing authority as soon as possible. The notice shall include the subjects expected to be considered at the meeting. In addition, the minutes shall reflect the reason for the emergency meeting, and the nature of the notice given to the media. 
(Res. of 5-14-96, § 1-16) 
Sec. 2-30. - Executive sessions. 
Executive sessions of the board may be held for the purpose of conducting business excepted from public access requirements as authorized by §§ 50-14-2 and 50-14-3 of the Official Code of Georgia Annotated. Where a meeting of the board is devoted in part to matters within the authorized exceptions to public access requirements, any portion of the meeting not subject to any such exceptions shall be open to the public. 
No executive session shall be held except pursuant to a majority affirmative vote of the board of commissioners taken in a public meeting. The minutes of the public meeting shall reflect the names of the commissioners present, those voting for the executive session and the specific reasons for the executive session. Minutes of the executive session may be maintained by the clerk of the board of commissioners at the direction of the chairman. Any such minutes shall be maintained in a confidential file and shall not be subject to disclosure, except that disclosures of such portions of minutes identifying real estate to be acquired by the board may be delayed only until such time as the acquisition of the real estate has been completed, terminated, or abandoned, or court proceedings have been initiated. 
(Res. of 5-14-96, § 1-17) 
Sec. 2-31. - Chairman. 
The chairman of the board of commissioners is responsible for the orderly conduct of the meeting. In order to fulfill this duty, the chairman must enforce the rules of procedure that are adopted by the board of commissioners. The chairman shall be impartial and shall conduct the meetings in a fair manner. 
(Res. of 5-14-96, § 1-05) 
Sec. 2-32. - Vice-chairman. 
The board shall select a vice-chairman from the board members at the beginning of each calendar year. The vice-chairman shall fulfill the duties of the chairman if the chairman is not in attendance. If the chairman and vice-chairman are absent and a quorum is present, the remaining commissioners shall select a commissioner to serve as temporary chairman of the meeting until either the chairman or vice-chairman is present at the meeting. 
(Res. of 5-14-96, § 1-06) 
Sec. 2-33. - Parliamentarian. 
The county attorney shall serve as the parliamentarian for board meetings. 
(Res. of 5-14-96, § 1-12) 
Sec. 2-34. - Quorum. 
A quorum must be present for conducting meetings of the board. A quorum is a majority of all of the members of the board then in office. It is the duty of the chairman to enforce this rule. Any commissioner may raise a point of order directed to the chairman if he or she believes that a quorum is not present. If, during the course of a meeting, a commissioner leaves and a quorum no longer exists, the meeting cannot continue. If a quorum is not attained within thirty minutes, the meeting will be rescheduled by the chairman with the approval of the commissioners present. 
(Res. of 5-14-96, § 1-02) 
Sec. 2-35. - Voting; majority. 
Passage of any motion shall require the affirmative vote of a majority of commissioners. 
(Res. of 5-14-96, § 1-03) 
Sec. 2-36. - Abstentions. 
A commissioner may abstain from voting on any motion. The commissioner shall explain for the record his or her decision to abstain on any vote. 
(Res. of 5-14-96, § 1-04) 
Sec. 2-37. - Decorum. 
All commissioners must conduct themselves in a professional and respectful manner. All remarks should be directed to the chairman and not to individual commissioners, staff or citizens in attendance. Personal remarks are inappropriate. A commissioner may not speak at a meeting until he has been recognized by the chairman. All comments made by a commissioner shall address the motion that is being discussed. The chairman shall enforce these rules of decorum. If a commissioner believes that a rule has been broken, he can raise a point of order. A second is not required. The chairman can rule on the question or allow the board to debate the issue and decide the issue by majority vote. 
(Res. of 5-14-96, § 1-10) 
Sec. 2-38. - Agenda. 
The county administrator, with the advice of the chairman and the commissioners, shall prepare an agenda of subjects to be acted on for each meeting. The agenda shall be made available to the commissioners at least one business day before every board meeting. Members of the public may request that a particular subject be placed on the agenda for the following regular monthly meeting scheduled for the second Tuesday of each month. To be considered, this request must be submitted to the county administrator no later than 3:00 p.m. on the Thursday preceding the first Tuesday of each month. 
(Res. of 5-14-96, § 1-07; Ord. of 6-9-09) 
Sec. 2-39. - Minutes. 
The clerk of the board shall promptly record the minutes for each board meeting. The minutes shall serve as the official written record of the board meeting and shall be open for public inspection once approved as official by the board, but in no case later than immediately following the next regular meeting of the board. The minutes shall specify the names of commissioners present at the meeting, a description of each motion or other proposal made at the meeting, the commissioner who proposed each motion, the commissioner who seconded each motion, and a record of all votes. In the case of a roll-call vote, the name of each commissioner voting for or against a proposal shall be recorded. It shall be presumed that a commissioner has voted in the affirmative unless the minutes show otherwise. More detailed formation may be included in the minutes at the request of the board. 
The board must approve the minutes before they can be considered as an official record of the board. A copy of the minutes from the previous meeting shall be distributed to the commissioners at least one business day before the following meeting. The minutes of the previous meeting shall be corrected and approved by the board at the beginning of each meeting. A majority vote is required for approval. Conflicts about the content of the minutes shall be decided by majority vote. Upon being approved, the minutes shall be signed by the chairman and attested to by the clerk of the board of commissioners. 
(Res. of 5-14-96, § 1-08) 
Sec. 2-40. - Order of business. 
All regular board meetings should follow an established order of business. The order is as follows: 
I.  Call to Order 
II.  Consent Agenda 
III.  Agenda 
IV.  Minutes 
V.  Announcements and Updates 
VI.  Appearances 
VII.  Old Business 
VIII.  New Business 
IX.  Executive Session (if needed) 
X.  Adjournment 
(Res. of 5-14-96, § 1-09; Ord. of 6-9-09) 
Sec. 2-41. - Amendments to rules. 
Any amendments to the rules of order must be submitted by a commissioner in writing to the county administrator at least three business days before a regular meeting of the board. The proposed amendment shall be included in the agenda for that meeting and distributed to all board members. All amendments shall require a 2/3 vote of the board to be adopted. 
(Res. of 5-14-96, § 1-13) 
Sec. 2-42. - Suspending the rules of order. 
Rules of order may be suspended in the case of an emergency. A motion to suspend the rules requires a second, is debatable and requires a 2/3 vote of the board. Rules governing quorum (section 2-34), voting methods and requirements (sections 2-35 and 2-36), the notification to commissioners of meetings (sections 2-29 and 2-30) and rules necessary for compliance with state law cannot be suspended. 
(Res. of 5-14-96, § 1-18) 
Sec. 2-43. - Public participation. 
Public participation in meetings of the board of commissioners shall be permitted in accordance with the provisions of this section. 
(1)  Public comments. The sixth agenda item of the regular monthly meeting shall be reserved for comments from the public. All members of the public who wish to address the board must submit their name and the topic of their comments to the county administrator no later than 3:00 p.m. on the Thursday preceding the first Tuesday of each month in order to be considered for placement on the agenda. Individuals who are placed on the agenda will be allotted five minutes each to make comments, and the comments must be limited to the designated topic. These limits may be waived by a majority vote of the board. 
(2)  Public participation on agenda items. By a majority vote, the board may allow public comment on an agenda item at the time the item is being considered by the board. These comments must be limited to the subject that is being debated. Members of the public may speak for five minutes and may speak only once. These limits can be waived by a majority vote of the board. Anyone wishing to speak at an any board meeting must be recognized by the chairman before addressing the board. 
(3)  Decorum. Members of the public shall not make inappropriate or offensive comments at a board meeting and are expected to comply with the rules of decorum that are established for commissioners. Individuals who violate any rules of the board may be ruled out of order by the chairman or on a point of order made by a commissioner. A majority vote of the board will rule on the point of order. An individual who violates the rules of decorum may be removed from the meeting at the direction of the chairman. 
(4)  Public hearings. The Board may schedule public hearings for the purpose of soliciting public comment on any subject of interest to the board. Hearings may be held immediately prior to or following a meeting of the board or at such other places and times as the board may determine. No official action shall be taken at any such public hearing. 
(Res. of 5-14-96, § 1-11; Ord. of 6-9-09) 
Sec. 2-44. - Committees. 
The chairman, with the concurrence of the board, may create committees of members of the board to study any issue before the board. Any such committees may make recommendations to the board, but no committee shall be empowered to make a final decision on any matter before it for consideration. In addition to board members, committees may include other county officials, staff or citizens at large. Whenever a committee is created, its duties, any limitation on the scope of its duties, and the times, places and periods of time for which the committee may operate shall be determined by the chairman with the concurrence of the board. The chairman shall be an ex officio member of all committees. 
(Res. of 5-14-96, § 1-19) 
Sec. 2-45. - Visual and sound recordings. 
Visual, sound, and visual and sound recordings shall be permitted for all public meetings. 
(Res. of 5-14-96, § 1-20) 
Secs. 2-46—2-50. - Reserved.

Footnotes:

Related laws reference— Water and sewerage authority, art. III.

DIVISION 2. - DEVELOPMENT AUTHORITY[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
Editor's note— The Peach County Industrial Development Authority created pursuant to 1969 Ga. Laws, page 2695 is no longer active. 
State Law reference— Development Authorities Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-62-1 et seq.; Resource Recovery Development Authorities Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-63-1 et seq.; Downtown Development Authorities Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-42-1 et seq.; Georgia Development Authority Act, O.C.G.A. § 50-10-1 et seq. 

Sec. 2-61. - Declaration of necessity. 
There is hereby determined and declared to be a pressing, existing and future need for a development authority, as more fully described and defined in the development authority law, to function in the county for the purpose of developing and promoting for the public good and general welfare trade, commerce, industry and employment opportunities in the county, thereby promoting the general welfare of the citizenry. 
(Res. of 12-14-76) 
Sec. 2-62. - Creation; authority. 
There is hereby activated in the county the public body corporate and politic known as the Development Authority of Peach County which was created upon the adoption and approval of the Development Authorities Law as set forth in O.C.G.A. § 36-62-1 et seq. 
(Res. of 12-14-76) 
Sec. 2-63. - Terms of directors. 
Directors shall serve in such capacity for six years. If at the end of any term of office of any director, a successor thereto shall not have been elected, then the director whose term of office shall have expired shall continue to hold office until his successor shall be so elected. 
(Res. of 12-14-76) 
Sec. 2-64. - Duties and powers. 
The elected board of directors shall organize itself, carry out its duties and responsibilities and exercise its powers and prerogatives in accordance with the terms and provisions of the Development Authorities Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-62-1 et seq. 
(Res. of 12-14-76) 
Sec. 2-65. - Actions of board of commissioners not to affect county development authority. 
Action taken by the board of commissioners, as specified in this division, is not intended in any way to affect the Peach County Development Authority, including, without limitations, its existence, purpose, organization, powers or function. 
(Res. of 12-14-76) 
Secs. 2-66—2-75. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - MIDDLE GEORGIA REGIONAL SOLID WASTE MANAGEMENT AUTHORITY[5] 

Footnotes: 
--- (5) --- 
Editor's note— An official copy of the agreement referred to in this division is on file in the office of the clerk of the board of commissioners. The participants are identified in such agreement as Doolg County, Macon County, and Peach County. 
Cross reference— Solid waste, ch. 38. 

Sec. 2-76. - Activation of authority. 
The county, after diligent study and review, hereby joins with the other participants in finding and declaring that there is a need for an authority to function in the area of solid waste management. In conjunction with the other participants, the county hereby activates the Middle Georgia Regional Solid Waste Management Authority, referred to in this division as "the authority," a public corporation created as an institution of purely public charity, to perform an essential governmental function in the exercise of the power conferred upon it by this division and the Regional Solid Waste Management Authority Act as set forth in O.C.G.A. § 12-8-50 et seq. 
(Res. of 8-30-93, § 1) 
Sec. 2-77. - Authorization of agreement among participants. 
Under the authority of Ga. Const. art. 9, sec. 3, par. 1, the execution, delivery and performance by the county of an agreement, dated July 27, 1993, between and among the county and each of the participants and the authority is hereby authorized. The execution of the agreement by the chairman of the board of commissioners, which is hereby authorized, shall be conclusive evidence of such approval. The agreement shall provide for the activation of the authority and the relationship between and among the participants, including the county, and establish on a preliminary basis the powers and duties of the authority relating to research, study, and planning for projects for the management of solid waste on behalf of the participants. The agreement shall only become effective upon its execution by two counties pursuant to the authorization of such execution through duly adopted resolutions. 
(Res. of 8-30-93, § 3) 
Sec. 2-78. - Other actions. 
In order to carry out the formation and activation of the authority, the chairman of the board of commissioners is further authorized to take any and all further action and execute and deliver any and all other documents that may be necessary or desirable in the execution, delivery, performance, or approval of the agreement and in order to carry out and effectuate fully the purposes thereof and hereof. 
(Res. of 8-30-93, § 4) 
Secs. 2-79—2-90. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - HOSPITAL AUTHORITY[6] 

Footnotes: 
--- (6) --- 
Related laws reference— Hospital authority, art. II. 
State Law reference— Creation of hospital authority in each county and municipality, O.C.G.A. § 31-7-72. 

Sec. 2-91. - Declaration of need. 
(a)  It is hereby determined and declared that there is a need for a hospital authority to function in the county. 
(b)  Such hospital authority is hereby established and created in accordance with the Hospital Authorities Law as set forth in O.C.G.A. § 31-7-70 et seq. 
(c)  Such hospital authority shall be known as the Hospital Authority of Peach County, referred to in this division as the "hospital authority." 
(Res. of 9-24-49, § 1) 
Sec. 2-92. - Exercise of powers. 
The hospital authority is authorized to exercise the powers contained in the Hospital Authorities Law, O.C.G.A. § 31-7-70 et seq., with respect to the area embraced within the county. 
(Res. of 9-24-49, § 2) 
Sec. 2-93. - Board of trustees. 
The board of trustees for the hospital authority shall consist of nine citizens of the county, who shall have all the rights, powers, privileges and authority, and be subject to the duties as provided by the Hospital Authorities Law, O.C.G.A. § 31-7-70 et seq. In addition, there shall be one honorary member of the board of trustees, who shall be the chief of staff of the Peach County Hospital or his designate. Such honorary member shall not be entitled to vote on any matter coming before the board of trustees, shall be disregarded in determining whether a quorum exists at any meeting and shall not otherwise be deemed a member of the board of trustees for any purpose, but shall be entitled to receive notice of and attend all meetings of the board of trustees. 
(Res. of 9-24-49, § 3; Res. of 5-13-75, § 1; Res. of 5-10-77, § 1) 
Sec. 2-94. - Ex officio members. 
The board of trustees of the hospital authority shall consist of two ex officio members and seven appointive or elective members. 
(Res. of 9-24-49, § 4; Res. of 5-13-75, § 2; Res. of 5-10-77, § 2) 
Sec. 2-95. - Designation of chairman. 
The two ex officio members of the hospital authority shall be the chairman of the board of commissioners of the county or his designate from the board of commissioners of the county and the mayor of the City of Fort Valley or his designate from the city council of the City of Fort Valley. Each of the ex officio members and/or designates shall have the same rights, powers, privileges and authority, including voting privileges, as the appointive or elective members. 
(Res. of 9-24-49, § 5; Res. of 5-13-75, § 3; Res. of 5-10-77, § 3) 
Secs. 2-96—2-100. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 5. - RECREATION COMMISSION[7] 

Footnotes: 
--- (7) --- 
Editor's note— Act. No. 199, adopted on April 13, 2007 did not specifically amend the Code; hence, at the discretion of the editor these provisions have been included as §§ 2-100.8—2-100.25. See also the Code Comparative Table. 

Sec. 2-100.1. - Established. 
Pursuant to the provisions of 1946 Ga. Laws, page 152, as amended, there is hereby established a recreation commission to be known as the Fort Valley-Byron-Peach County Recreation Commission, referred to in this division as the "recreation commission." 
(Ord. of 9-27-76, § 1) 
Sec. 2-100.2. - Membership. 
The recreation commission shall consist of seven persons serving without pay, three of whom shall be appointed by the mayor and council of the City of Fort Valley, three of whom shall be appointed by the chairman and the board of commissioners of the county and one of whom shall be appointed by the mayor and council of the City of Byron. 
(Ord. of 9-27-76, § 2) 
Sec. 2-100.3. - Terms; vacancies. 
The term of office for members of the recreation commission shall be five years or until their successors are appointed and qualified, except that the members of the commission first appointed shall be appointed for such terms that the term of one member shall expire annually thereafter. Vacancies in such commission occurring otherwise than by expiration of the term shall be filled by another appointment for the unexpired term. 
(Ord. of 9-27-76, § 3) 
Sec. 2-100.4. - Officers; adoption of bylaws. 
Immediately after their appointment, the members of the recreation commission shall meet and organize by electing one of their members president and such other officers as may be necessary. The commission shall have power to adopt bylaws, rules and regulations, subject to the approval of the appointive bodies, for the proper conduct of recreation for such cities and county. 
(Ord. of 9-27-76, § 4) 
Sec. 2-100.5. - Powers and duties. 
The recreation commission shall have all the powers and perform all duties designated by 1946 Ga. Laws, page 152, as now or hereafter amended. 
(Ord. of 9-27-76, § 5) 
Sec. 2-100.6. - Budget; gifts and bequests. 
The recreation commission shall submit an annual budget to the governing authorities of the City of Fort Valley, the county and the City of Byron for approval. The commission may also solicit or receive any gifts or bequests of money or other personal property or a donation to be applied, principal or income, for either temporary or permanent use for playgrounds or other recreational purposes. 
(Ord. of 9-27-76, § 6) 
Sec. 2-100.7. - Reports. 
The recreation commission shall make an annual report of its activities to the governing boards and such other reports as from time to time may be required. 
(Ord. of 9-27-76, § 7) 
Sec. 2-100.8. - Creation of board. 
Pursuant to subsection (b) of O.C.G.A. Section 21-2-40, there is created the Board of Elections and Registration of Peach County, hereinafter referred to as "the board." The board shall have the powers, duties, and responsibilities of the judge of the probate court of Peach County under Chapter 2 of Title 21 of the O.C.G.A., the "Georgia Election Code," and the powers, duties, and responsibilities of the board of registrars of Peach County under Chapter 2 of Title 21 of the O.C.G.A., the "Georgia Election Code." 
(Act of 4-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-100.9. - Terms. 
The terms "election," "elector," "political party," "primary," and "public office" shall have the same meanings as set forth in Chapter 2 of Title 21 of the O.C.G.A., the "Georgia Election Code," unless otherwise clearly apparent from the text of this Act, and the term "board" means the Board of Elections and Registration of Peach County, "commissioners" means the Board of Commissioners of Peach County, and "county" means Peach County. 
(Act of 4-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-100.10. - The board. 
(a)  The board shall be composed of five members who shall be appointed as provided in this section. 
(b)  Two members of the board shall be appointed by the governing authority of Peach County. 
(c)  One member of the board shall be selected by the county executive committee of the political party which received the highest number of votes within the county for its candidate for governor in the general election immediately preceding the appointment of such member. 
(d)  One member of the board shall be selected by the county executive committee of the political party which received the second highest number of votes within the county for its candidate for governor in the general election immediately preceding the appointment of such member. 
(e)  One member shall be selected by the chief judge of the Superior Court of Peach County. 
(f)  All appointments to the board shall be promptly certified by the appointing authority to the clerk of the Superior Court of Peach County. 
(g)  The initial appointees to the board shall take office on October 1, 2007. The two members appointed by the governing authority of Peach County and the member selected by the chief judge of the Superior Court of Peach County shall serve terms beginning on October 1, 2007, and ending on September 30, 2011, and until his or her respective successor is duly appointed and qualified. Successors to each such member shall thereafter be appointed by the appropriate appointing authority to serve a term of office of four years beginning October 1, 2011, and until their successors are duly appointed and qualified. The two appointees of the political parties shall serve a term beginning on October 1, 2007, and ending on September 30, 2009, and until his or her respective successor is duly appointed and qualified. Successors to such members shall thereafter be appointed by the appropriate appointing authority to serve a term of office of four years beginning October 1, 2009, and until their respective successors are duly appointed and qualified. Thereafter, all members shall be appointed to serve four year terms of office and until their successors are duly appointed and qualified. 
(Act of 4-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-100.11. - Election supervisor. 
The Peach County Board of Commissioners, which will consider the recommendation of the Board of Elections and Registration of Peach County, shall be authorized to appoint a person to serve as the election supervisor of Peach County. The Peach County Board of Commissioners shall set the salary and employment status of the election supervisor, said salary to be payable from county funds. If appointed, the election supervisor shall generally direct and control the administration of the affairs of the board pursuant to law and duly adopted resolutions of the board. The election supervisor shall not be a member of the board. The election supervisor shall be supervised by the board and shall be deemed to be an at-will employee of the Board of Commissioners of Peach County and shall be subject to removal from office, with or without cause, by the Board of Commissioners of Peach County. 
(Act of 4-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-100.12. - Members of the board. 
Each member of the board shall: 
(1)  Be eligible to be reappointed to succeed such member; 
(2)  Have the right to resign at any time by giving written notice of such resignation to the governing authority of Peach County and to the clerk of the Superior Court of Peach County; 
(3)  Serve until his or her successor is appointed and qualified; and 
(4)  Be subject to removal from the board by the chief judge of the Superior Court of Peach County at any time, for cause, after notice and hearing. 
(Act of 4-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-100.13. - Appointing authority. 
(a)  The appointing authority shall certify the appointment of each member of the board by filing an affidavit with the clerk of the Superior Court of Peach County no later than 30 days preceding the date upon which such members are to take office, stating the name and residential address of the person appointed and certifying such member has been duly appointed as provided in this Act. 
(b)  The clerk of the superior court shall record each of such certifications on the minutes of the superior court and shall certify the name of each such appointed member to the Secretary of State and provide for the issuance of appropriate commissions to the members within the same time and in the same manner as provided by law for registrars. 
(Act of 4-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-100.14. - Vacancies. 
In the event a vacancy occurs in the office of any member before the expiration of his or her term, by removal, death, resignation, or otherwise, the appointing authority which is required under section 2-100.10 of this Act to make the appointment to the office upon the expiration of the term shall appoint a successor to serve the remainder of the unexpired term as provided for in section 2-100.10 of this Act. If the vacancy in office is not filled within 60 days after it occurs, the vacancy shall be filled for the remainder of the term by the governing authority of Peach County. The clerk of the superior court shall be notified of such interim appointments and record and certify such appointments in the same manner as the regular appointment of members. 
(a)  The first members of the board under this Act shall be appointed as provided in this Act to take office on October 1, 2007. The board shall take no official action until all members have been certified to the clerk of the Superior Court of Peach County. 
(b)  Before entering upon the member's duties, each member shall take substantially the same oath as required by law for registrars and shall have the same privileges from arrest. 
(Act of 4-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-100.15. - Terms of elective public office. 
(a)  No person who holds elective public office shall be eligible to serve as a member of the board during the term of such elective office, and the position of any member of the board shall be deemed vacant upon such member's qualifying as a candidate for elective public office. 
(b)  Members of the board must be residents of Peach County and must have been registered voters in Peach County for a period of at least one year prior to the date of their appointment to the board. 
(Act of 4-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-100.16. - Joint primaries. 
(a)  Nothing in this Act shall be construed to require or prohibit joint primaries or to require or prohibit the commissioners or any other public agency to bear any expense of conducting primaries not otherwise required by law. 
(b)  The board shall have the authority to contract with any municipality located within Peach County for the holding by the board of any primary or election to be conducted within such municipality. 
(Act of 4-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-100.17. - Expending public funds. 
With the approval of the commissioners, the board shall be authorized to expend public funds for the purpose of preparing and distributing material solely to inform and instruct electors of the county adequately with regard to elections. No material distributed by the board shall contain or express, in any manner or form, any commentary or expression of opinion or request for support with respect to any political issue or matter of political concern. 
(Act of 4-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-100.18. - Management of the board's affairs. 
(a)  The board shall be authorized and empowered to organize itself, elect its officers from among its members, determine its procedural rules and regulations, adopt bylaws, specify the functions and duties of its employees, and otherwise take such action as is appropriate to the management of its affairs; provided, however, that no such action shall conflict with state law. 
(Act of 4-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-100.19. - Duties of the board. 
(a)  The board shall fix and establish, by appropriate resolution entered on its minutes, directives governing the execution of matters within its jurisdiction. The board shall hold meetings at the county courthouse or at the place of meeting of the commissioners. Any specially called meetings held pursuant to the bylaws adopted by the board shall be held only after notification of the time and place or the holding of such special meeting has been communicated in writing to provide public notice of the meeting as required by law. All meetings of whatever kind of the board shall be conducted pursuant to Chapter 14 of Title 50 of the O.C.G.A. 
(b)  The board shall maintain a written record of policy decisions amended to include additions or deletions. Such written records shall be made available for the public to review pursuant to Article 4 of Chapter 18 of Title 50 of the O.C.G.A. 
(Act of 4-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-100.20. - Compensation of the members of the board. 
(a)  Compensation for the members of the board shall be fixed by the commissioners. 
(b)  All amounts payable under this section shall be paid from the funds of Peach County. 
(Act of 4-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-100.21. - Clerical assistants of the board. 
(a)  The board may request additional clerical assistants as needed to carry out efficiently the duties and functions of the board on either an independent contract basis or as county employees, to be determined by the commissioners. The commissioners shall be responsible for determining the pay and salary of all clerical assistants of the board. Any such assistants shall be hired by the commissioners, which shall consider the recommendation of the board, and such clerical assistants shall be at-will employees of the commissioners. 
(b)  The commissioners shall provide suitable offices and equipment and funding sufficient to employ the staff and other employees as may be necessary. 
(Act of 4-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-100.22. - Poll workers. 
The board shall be responsible for the selection, appointment, and training of poll workers. 
(Act of 4-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-100.23. - Preclearance. 
The commissioners shall cause, through its legal counsel, this Act to be submitted for preclearance under Section 5 of the federal Voting Rights Act of 1965, as amended, within 45 days after the date on which this Act is approved by the governor or otherwise becomes law without such approval. 
(Act of 4-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-100.24. - Effective date. 
This Act shall become effective upon its approval by the governor or upon its becoming law without such approval for purposes of making initial appointments to the board only. This Act shall become fully effective on October 1, 2007. Upon this Act becoming fully effective, the current superintendent of elections of Peach County the judge of the probate court of Peach County, and the existing board of registrars of Peach County shall be relieved of all powers and duties to which the board succeeds by the provisions of this Act and shall deliver to the board all equipment, supplies, materials, books, papers, records, and facilities pertaining to such powers and duties. Nothing contained herein is intended to prevent the appointment of members of the board, the appointment of an election supervisor, the hiring of clerical staff, or any necessary training for the members of the board, the election supervisor and clerical assistants prior to October 1, 2007. 
(Act of 4-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-100.25. - Repealer. 
All laws and parts of laws in conflict with this Act are repealed. 
(Act of 4-13-2007) 
Secs. 2-100.26—2-100.126. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - FINANCE 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Secs. 2-101—2-110. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - PURCHASING[8] 

Footnotes: 
--- (8) --- 
State Law reference— Power of expenditure, Ga. Const. art. 9, sec. 4, par. 2; discretion of municipal governing body as to management and disposition of property, O.C.G.A. § 36-30-2; acquisition, sale and lease by municipality of real and personal property, O.C.G.A. § 36-37-1 et seq.; disposition of municipal property, O.C.G.A. § 36-37-6; multiyear lease, purchase or lease purchase contracts, O.C.G.A. § 36-60-13; local political subdivision purchases, O.C.G.A. § 50-5-100 et seq. 

Sec. 2-111. - Intent. 
It is the intent of the board of commissioners to establish regulations and procedures to provide for an efficient and fiscally responsible system for the purchase of materials and services necessary for the effective operations of the county government and to ensure the administration of such system is in accordance with the highest ethical and fiscal standards and applicable laws. 
(Ord. of 10-26-1993, § I; Ord. of 12-14-2010) 
Sec. 2-112. - Applicability. 
The provisions of this division shall apply to all primary departments and agencies receiving appropriations from the board of commissioners and to other agencies as the board of commissioners may deem appropriate. 
(Ord. of 10-26-1993, § II) 
Sec. 2-113. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Account number means the number assigned to a specific account title in a classification of accounts. For the county, this number includes a three-digit fund designation, a five-digit department designation, and a six-digit object/expenditure designation. 
Accounting system means all the records, formal and informal, together with the procedures that have to do with assembling the financial operations and condition of a governmental unit. 
Accounts payable means liabilities on open account owing to private persons, firms, or corporations, or to governmental units. 
Acknowledgement means a form used by a vendor to inform a purchaser that his order has been received. It generally implies vendor's acceptance. 
Alternate bids means the amount stated in the bid or proposal to be added to or deducted from the amount of the base bid or base proposal if the corresponding change in project scope or alternate materials or methods of construction is accepted. 
Appropriation means an authorization granted by the board of commissioners to make expenditures or to incur obligations for specific purposes. 
As is means an expression signifying that goods offered for sale are without warranty or guarantee. The purchaser has no recourse on the vendor for the quality or condition of the goods. 
Back order means the undelivered part of a previous order, which the vendor re-enters for shipment at a later date. 
Base bid or base proposal means the amount of money stated in the bid or proposal as the sum for which the bidder or proposer offers to perform the work. 
Bid means a price offer by a prospective purchaser, for example, an auction bid or a quotation given, usually in competition with other vendors, in response to an intending buyer's request. 
Bid bond means a bond with good and sufficient surety or sureties for the faithful acceptance of the contract payable to, in favor of, and for the protection of Peach County for which the contract is awarded. 
Blanket purchases means an open purchase order to a particular vendor covering certain materials and supplies for a stated period of time. 
Brand name means an arbitrarily adopted name that is given by a manufacturer or merchant to an article or service to distinguish it as produced or sold by him and that may be used and protected as a trademark. 
Budget amendment means a change in the overall appropriation granted by the board of commissioners to a particular government department (user agency). This requires approval by the board of commissioners. 
Budget transfer means moving a portion of a line item appropriation to another line item within a department's total budget appropriation. The total budget appropriation for that department does not change. This requires approval by the board of commissioners' county clerk. 
Cash in advance means payment is to accompany purchaser's order. 
Change order means an alteration, addition, or deduction from the original scope of work as defined by the contract documents to address changes or unforeseen conditions necessary for project completion. 
Competitive sealed bidding means a method of soliciting bids, generally received in a sealed envelope to protect the confidentiality of the bid until a specified time and place for opening, whereby the award is based upon the lowest responsive, responsible bid in conformance with bidding rules and specifications. 
Competitive sealed proposals means a method of soliciting proposals, generally received in a sealed envelope to protect the confidentiality of the bid until a specified time and place for opening, whereby the award is based upon criteria identified in a request for proposals in conformance with bidding rules and specifications. 
Confirming order (confirmation) means a purchase order listing the goods or services and terms of an order originally placed orally. 
Contract means an oral or written, legally binding mutual agreement between two competent parties. An accepted purchase order becomes a contract. 
Date needed means the date the department needs the material or service. A definite date must be given since this may affect the price. 
Delivery means the transfer of possession. In shipping, it occurs when the carrier submits the bill of lading or title to the goods to the recipient. 
Delivery schedule means the agreed time or rate of future deliveries of purchased goods or services. 
Depreciation means decrease in value of a capital asset because of use, deterioration, inadequacy, or obsolescence. 
Discount means an amount deducted from the selling price by the vendor. It is generally applied when a purchaser meets stipulations that reduce the cost of the goods, for example: quantity discounts. 
Emergency means any situation resulting in imminent danger to the public health or safety or the loss of an essential governmental service. 
Emergency purchase means when a purchase is made due to conditions that exist that present a threat to the safety, health, and welfare of the citizens of the county and whenever such requirements would cause an undue delay in the delivery of essential county services under such conditions. 
Encumbrances means obligations in the form of purchase orders, contracts, or salary commitments, which are chargeable to an appropriation and for which a part of the appropriation is reserved. 
Equipment means physical property of a more or less permanent nature, other than land, buildings, or improvements to land or buildings, ordinarily useful in carrying on operations. Examples are machinery, tools, trucks, cars, furniture, and furnishings. 
Expedite means to execute promptly or to accelerate the process or progress of. 
Inspection means the act of examining and scrutinizing something to determine if a particular standard is met. The inspection of a delivery of goods or services should determine the condition, quality, quantity, acceptability, and completeness of the goods or services received. 
Inventory means a stock of goods or an itemized list of a stock of goods on hand at a particular time. When ascertained by a physical count of the items, it is a physical inventory. When determined from records maintained for routine business activities, it is a book inventory. 
Invitation to bid means a request made by a purchaser to prospective suppliers for their competitive price quotations on goods or services. 
Invoice means a bill sent to a buyer for payment. It shows quantity, price, and nature of goods or services delivered. 
Lead time means the period of time between that of ordering to the date of delivery that a buyer must reasonably grant the vendor to prepare goods for shipment. 
Payment bond means a bond with good and sufficient surety or sureties payable to Peach County for which the work is to be done and intended for the use and protection of all subcontractors and all persons supplying labor, materials, machinery, and equipment in the prosecution of the work provided for in the contract. 
Performance bond means a bond with good and sufficient surety or sureties for the faithful performance of the contract and to indemnify Peach County for any damages occasioned by a failure to perform the same within the prescribed time. Such bond shall be payable to, in favor of, and for the protection of Peach County for which the work is to be done. 
Petty cash means a sum of money, in the form of currency, set aside and controlled for the purpose of making immediate reimbursement payments of comparatively small amounts for authorized purchases. 
Price schedule means a list of prices applying to varying quantities or kinds of goods. 
Procurement means to get possession of or to obtain by particular care and effort. 
Public works construction means the building, altering, repairing, improving, or demolishing of any public structure or building or other public improvements of any kind to any public real property. Such term does not include the routine operation, repair, or maintenance of existing structures, buildings, or real property. 
Purchase means to acquire property or services for a price. 
Purchase order means a purchaser's formal written offer to a vendor containing all terms and conditions of a proposed transaction. The purchase order authorizes a vendor to deliver specified merchandise and to make a charge therefore. 
Purchase order number means a unique number assigned to a purchase order for recording and tracking all transactions related to that order. 
Purchase requisition means a formal request made to purchasing by a user agency to procure goods or services from vendors. 
Quotation means a statement of price, terms of sale, and description of goods or services offered by a vendor to a prospective purchaser; a bid. When given in response to an inquiry, it is generally considered a sales proposal. It also means the stating of the current price of a commodity. 
Rebate means a sum of money returned by a vendor to a purchaser in consideration of the purchase of a specified quantity or value of goods usually within a stated interval. 
Receiving report means a document used by a department to inform others in the company of the receipt of purchased goods. For the county, the receiving report is a copy of the purchase order with the signature of the authorized department official showing completeness and acceptability of the order. 
Requisition number means an identification number for tracking requisitions for purchase. 
Responsible bidder (responsible offeror) means a person or entity that has the capability in all respects to perform fully and reliably the contract requirements. 
Responsive bidder (responsive offeror) means a person or entity that has submitted a bid or proposal that conforms in all material respects to the requirements set forth in the invitation for bids or request for proposals. 
Restricted purchase order means an official government purchase order, which receives its authority by a department head's signature and is valid only for purchases of less than $500.00. 
Sales tax means a tax levied upon a vendor's sale. The county is exempt from paying sales tax. 
Sample means a small portion of goods taken as a specimen of quality. 
Scope of project means the work required by the original contract documents and any subsequent change orders required or appropriate to accomplish the intent of the project as described in the bid documents. 
Scope of work means the work that is required by the contract documents. 
Sealed bid. See "Competitive sealed bidding." 
Seller's lien means the right of a seller to retain possession of goods until payment is received except where goods are sold on credit. 
Sole source means those procurements made pursuant to a written determination by the county that there is only one source for the required supply, service, or construction item due to specific scientific technology or extraordinary specifications and circumstances. 
Specifications means a comprehensive and accurate statement of the technical and procedural requirements of requested goods or services. Specifications should also include any procedures to be followed to ascertain if the requirements are met. 
Statement of account means a list, generally prepared by the vendor, detailing the transactions between vendor and purchaser for a stated period of time, usually a month, and concluding with the open or unpaid balance. 
Stock means the supply of goods maintained on hand to satisfy anticipated demand. 
Subcontractor means a party contracting with a prime contractor to perform all or any part of the latter's contract. 
Terms of payment means the method of payment agreed upon in a sales contract. The three basic terms are cash, open account, and secured account. 
Trade name. See "Brand name." 
Unit means order unit, such as feet, dozen, gallon, etc. 
Used means not new or secondhand. 
Vendor number means a number assigned to a particular vendor that references all of that vendor's information in the county government's computerized financial system. 
Voucher means a written certification, usually testifying that services have been performed or goods purchased and authorizing payment to be made to the vendor. 
Warranty means a written guarantee of the integrity of a product and of the maker's responsibility for the repair or replacement of defective parts. 
(Ord. of 10-26-1993; Amd. of 12-8-2009; Mo. of 4-6-2010; Ord. of 12-14-2010) 
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 2-114. - Purchasing manager. 
The purchasing manager is assigned the general duties and responsibilities of supervising and administering the provisions of this division. The purchasing manager's authority, responsibilities, and duties are, as follows: 
(1)  To carry out the policies, regulations, and procedures for purchasing all goods and services required by the user agencies of the county pursuant to the provisions of this division; and other directives of the board of commissioners not in conflict with this division. 
(2)  To obtain the highest quality of goods and services for the most economical costs which will provide the most effective operations of the county. 
(3)  To maintain up-to-date files of all vendors known to the board of commissioners who are reputable and responsible vendors of goods and services. 
(4)  To ensure that all purchases are in compliance with the county's budgeting and accounting policies and procedures. 
(5)  To make requests to the board of commissioners for declarations of ineligibility on any vendor that misrepresents or defaults on any quotation, bid, or purchase agreement with the county and disqualifying such vendor from doing further business with the county for a specified period of time. 
(6)  To promulgate policies and procedures to administer and carry out the provisions of this division or other policies established by the county pertaining to county governmental purchases. 
(7)  To ensure that all standards and specifications are reasonable, nonrestrictive when possible, and certain to promote open competition among vendors. 
(8)  To provide for a uniform purchasing manual which shall include rules and regulations pertaining to the purchasing of goods and services for Peach County and a step-by-step description of the proper procedures for purchasing those goods and services. The purchasing manual, as approved by the board of commissioners, shall be considered a part of this division by reference and shall have the same force and effect as this division. 
(9)  To review special needs of any user agency to identify noncompetitive types and kinds of goods and services and to exempt such items from certain purchasing procedures. Any such exemption shall include documentation of the reasons for the exemption. 
(10)  It shall be the responsibility of the purchasing manager to report any actual or suspected misuse of county property, supplies, or services to the board of commissioners. 
(11)  It shall be the responsibility of the purchasing manager to maintain a record and description, as a public record, of all requisitions, competitive bids and quotations, purchase orders, receiving reports, bid rejections, and other pertinent purchasing documentation, in accordance with the regulations and procedures prescribed in the purchasing manual. 
(Ord. of 10-26-1993, § III; Amd. of 12-8-2009) 
Sec. 2-115. - User agency. 
A user agency is any department, division, agency, bureau, commission, board, authority, or other unit of the county government using goods and services to carry out the duties and responsibilities of such functions and for which financial appropriations have been made by the board of commissioners. The user agency's authority, responsibilities, and duties are, as follows: 
(1)  To conduct the purchasing function within the user agency pursuant to the provisions of this division and the attached purchasing manual, to communicate these policies and procedures to user agency vendors when necessary, and to refer policy and procedure questions to the purchasing manager for resolution. 
(2)  To initiate the purchasing process for requested goods or services by the completion and submission of a requisition for purchase through the automated purchasing system as prescribed in the attached purchasing manual. 
(3)  To submit requests for purchases of goods and services, especially inventory replacement, in a timely manner to facilitate meeting the terms of this division and to hold emergency purchases to a minimum. 
(4)  To act responsibly and for the ultimate good of the county when utilizing the procedures for making emergency purchases and to complete and submit all paperwork and enter all required information in the automated purchasing system regarding the emergency purchase as specified in the attached purchasing manual. 
(5)  To provide suggested vendors and technical information and advice on goods and services requested. 
(6)  To keep an open file for purchase orders pending delivery of goods to the user agency, to inspect any shipments for accuracy and quality of condition, and to report the delivery to purchasing as per the procedures specified in the purchasing manual. 
(7)  The user agency will be ultimately responsible to the board of commissioners as to fund availability. 
(8)  To provide clear and valid written justification for any purchases requested from sole source vendors or where specifications are restricted as to brand name or features. 
(9)  To make recommendations for bid awards where quality and service are involved in addition to price, ensuring that the best interest of the county is served. 
(Ord. of 10-26-1993, § IV; Amd. of 12-8-2009) 
Sec. 2-116. - Award of contracts. 
(a)  The purchasing manager shall be authorized to award a contract for the purchase of goods and services to the most economical, best, and most responsible bidder or vendor when approved in the budget or approved project resolution up to $4,999.99. The approval of the board of commissioners shall be required before the award of a contract or purchase in excess of $5,000.00 is made. 
(b)  In addition to price, the board of commissioners and/or the purchasing manager shall consider the following: 
(1)  The ability, capacity, and skill of the bidder to perform the contract or provide the service required; 
(2)  Whether the bidder can perform the contract or provide the service promptly or within the time specified, without delay or interference; 
(3)  The character, integrity, reputation, judgment, experience, and efficiency of the bidder; 
(4)  The quality of performance of previous contracts of services or as determined from references; 
(5)  The previous and existing compliance by the bidder with laws and ordinances relating to the contract or service; 
(6)  The sufficiency of the financial resources and ability of the bidder to perform the contract or provide the service; 
(7)  The quality, availability, and adaptability of the supplies or contractual services to the particular use required; 
(8)  The ability of the bidder to provide future maintenance and service for the use of the subject of the contract; 
(9)  The number and scope of conditions attached to the bid; 
(10)  Whether the vendor is in default with the county as per section 2-127. 
(c)  Conflict of Interest. 
(1)  Neither the purchasing manager nor any employee, officer, agent, immediate family member, or board member of the county shall participate in the selection, award, or administration of a purchase or contract if a conflict of interest, real or apparent, would be involved. Such a conflict would arise when the purchasing manager, employee, officer, agent, immediate family member or board member has a financial or other interest in the firm selected for the award. 
(2)  Any employee, appointed officer, or elected officer of the county who is also an owner, employee, or any person who gains any form of financial benefit from any private company that engages in the sale of real or personal property to the county shall follow all purchasing and sealed bid requirements as directed by the county and shall make a full declaration of his or her status as an owner, employee, or any person who gains any form of financial benefit from any private company that engages in the sale of real or person property to the county. If the status of the employee, appointed officer, or elected officer of the county should change during the course of employment, appointment, or term, said employee, appointed officer, or elected officer shall file an updated declaration with the county purchasing manager within 15 days of said change of status. 
(Ord. of 10-26-1993, § V; Amd. of 12-8-2009; Ord. of 12-14-2010) 
Sec. 2-117. - Rejection of bids or quotations. 
The board of commissioners and/or the purchasing manager, as determined by the authority to award bids or quotations for contracts and/or purchases, shall be authorized to reject any or all bids, in whole or in part, when it is determined that the terms, conditions, or specifications received are not in compliance with those in the county bid solicitation. In such an event, the board of commissioners and/or the purchasing manager shall document the circumstances of such rejection and reissue the solicitation as appropriate. 
(Ord. of 10-26-1993, § VI; Amd. of 12-8-2009) 
Sec. 2-118. - Purchases of less than $2,500.00. 
Any supply, material, or contractual service which has an estimated cost of less than $2,500.00 may be purchased from any approved vendor recommended by the user agency or, in the absence of such recommendation, from any approved vendor selected by the purchasing manager. Each such purchase shall be authorized by the head of the user agency. Although multiple quotes are not required for purchases at this level, receiving multiple quotes as time allows is suggested for receiving the greatest cost savings for county government. 
(Ord. of 10-26-1993, § VII; Amd. of 12-8-2009; Ord. of 12-14-2010) 
Sec. 2-119. - Competitive quotations. 
(a)  Competitive quotations under $5,000.00. Any supply, material, or contractual service to be purchased by the county which has an estimated cost of not less than $2,500.00 but not more than $4,999.99 shall be purchased on the open market, without regard for formal advertising. Upon the receipt of documented written or oral price quotations from at least three reputable vendors for such item or service if three such vendors exist, the purchasing manager shall award the contract. The purchasing manager shall be authorized to reject any or all bids or quotations as per section 2-117. 
(b)  Competitive quotations under $10,000.00. Any supply, material, or contractual service to be purchased by the county which has an estimated cost of not less than $5,000.00 and not more than $10,000.00 shall be purchased on the open market, without regard for formal advertising. Upon receipt of documented written price quotations from at least three reputable vendors if three such vendors exist, the board of commissioners shall award the contract. The board of commissioners will be authorized to reject any or all bids or quotations as per section 2-117. 
(c)  Competitive quotations over $10,000.00. Any supply, material, or contractual service to be purchased by the county which has an estimated cost of more than $10,000.00 shall be purchased through formal sealed bids with formal advertising in the local and/or regional newspaper pursuant to sections 2-121 and 2-122. 
(Ord. of 10-26-1993, § VIII; Amd. of 12-8-2009; Ord. of 12-14-2010) 
Sec. 2-120. - Professional services. 
(a)  Professional services may be required on a project basis, for specific activities, or for certain durations of time. Procurement of these services shall be the primary responsibility of the user agency with the assistance of the purchasing manager. A contract for professional services shall be awarded to the best-qualified proposal based on the evaluation of the proposals and negotiation of reasonable and fair compensation for services. 
(b)  Professional service contracts which exceed a contract period of one year shall stipulate that the county may, at its own discretion, terminate said contract for cause or otherwise, at any time prior to the close of the contract period. Professional service needs shall be limited to a maximum of five years without again requesting proposals for such general services from the professional community unless expressly excepted by the board of commissioners. Services provided by some licensed professionals, such as practitioners of law, medicine, accountants, or professional consultants may not be subject to competitive bidding. Professional service contracts excluded from competitive bidding will be approved by the board of commissioners and will be considered on a case-by-case basis. 
(c)  The initial selection of such professional services shall be accomplished as outlined below. Fees for such services may be negotiated at the time of such designation or on a project/activities basis. 
(1)  Professional services which have an estimated cost of less than $2,500.00 may be purchased from any approved list of professionals recommended by the user agency or, in the absence of such recommendation, from any approved professional selected by the purchasing manager. Each such purchase shall be authorized by the head of the user agency. Any or all bids or quotations may be rejected as per section 2-117. 
(2)  Professional services which have an estimated cost of not less than $2,500.00 but not more than $4,999.99 shall be purchased on the open market, without regard for formal advertising. Upon the receipt of documented written or oral proposals from at least three qualified professionals for the service if three such professionals exist, the user agency shall select and the purchasing manager shall award the contract. Any or all bids or quotations may be rejected, as per section 2-117. 
(3)  Professional services which have an estimated cost of not less than $5,000.00 and not more than $10,000.00 shall be purchased on the open market, without regard for formal advertising. Upon receipt of written proposals from at least three qualified professionals of the service if three such professionals exist, the user agency with the assistance of the purchasing manager shall select and the board of commissioners shall award the contract. Any or all bids may be rejected, as per section 2-117. 
(4)  Professional services that have an estimated cost of more than $10,000.00 shall be purchased through a request for proposal. When determined appropriate by the board of commissioners, solicitation may be made through formal advertising in the local or regional newspapers, or any other similar means to notify the professional community. The user agency with assistance from the purchasing manager will make a recommended selection, and the board of commissioners shall award the contract. The board of commissioners reserves the right to reject any or all bids, as per section 2-117. 
(Ord. of 10-26-1993, § IX; Amd. of 12-8-2009; Ord. of 12-14-2010) 
Sec. 2-121. - Invitations to bid. 
(a)  Invitations to bid will be sent to at least three vendors where that many are available to provide the items or services required. 
(b)  Invitations to bid for projects expected to be in excess of $10,000.00 shall be by sealed bid and shall be published in the legal organ of the county for two consecutive weeks (except as noted in section 2-122. 
(c)  The legal advertisement of invitations for bids shall identify what item(s) are being bought, the date of the closing of the bids, time, date, and location of bid openings, the specifications for the project, equipment or service, or the location of such specifications. 
(d)  Bid openings will be made public, and the general public will be permitted to attend. Bid amounts submitted for public works contracts will not be made available to the public until it is determined by the board of commissioners that further negotiations will not be required. 
(e)  Bids, which are received after the designated time and date, will be considered null and void. 
(Ord. of 10-26-1993, § X; Amd. of 12-8-2009) 
Sec. 2-122. - Public works contracts. 
(a)  All public works construction contracts subject to this section entered into by the board of commissioners with private persons or entities shall be in writing and on file and available for public inspection in the office of the board of commissioners. 
(b)  (1)  Prior to entering into a public works construction contract other than those exempted by 2-122(g), the board of commissioners shall publicly advertise the contract opportunity. Such notice shall be posted conspicuously in the office of the board of commissioners and shall be advertised in the legal organ. All invitations for bids for public works contracts, i.e. improvements or additions to any county building, road, etc., in excess of $100,000.00 shall be by sealed bid and advertised in the legal organ a minimum of two times, with the first advertisement occurring at least four weeks prior to the opening of the sealed bids or proposals. The second advertisement shall follow no earlier than two weeks from the first advertisement. Notice of the contract shall also be posted on the courthouse door during the advertising period. 
(2)  Contract opportunities that will be awarded by competitive sealed bids shall have plans and specifications available on the first day of the advertisement and shall be open to inspection by the public. The plans and specifications shall indicate if the project will be awarded by base bid or base bid plus selected alternates, and: 
a.  A statement listing whether all anticipated federal, state, or local permits required for the project have been obtained or an indication of the status of the application for each such permit including when it is expected to be obtained; and 
b.  A statement listing whether all anticipated rights of way and easements required for the project have been obtained or an indication of the status as to when each such rights of way or easements are expected to be obtained. 
(3)  Contract opportunities that will be awarded by competitive sealed proposals shall be publicly advertised with a request for proposals which request shall include conceptual program information in the request for proposals describing the requested services in a level of detail appropriate to the project delivery method selected for the project. 
(4)  The advertisement shall include such details and specifications as will enable the public to know the extent and character of the work to be done. 
(5)  All required notices of advertisement shall also advise of any mandatory prequalification requirements or pre-bid conferences. Any advertisement which provides notice of a mandatory pre-bid conference or prequalification shall provide reasonable advance notice of said conference or for the submittal of such prequalification information. 
(c)  All public works construction contracts subject to the requirements of this section which place the bidder or offeror at risk for construction and require labor or building materials in the execution of the contract shall be awarded on the basis of competitive sealed bidding or competitive sealed proposals. The board of commissioners shall have the authority to reject all bids or proposals or any bid or proposal that is nonresponsive or not responsible and to waive technicalities and informalities. 
(d)  No addenda modifying plans and specifications shall be issued within a period of 72 hours prior to the advertised time for the opening of bids or proposals, excluding Saturdays, Sundays, and legal holidays. However, if the necessity arises to issue an addendum modifying plans and specifications within the 72-hour period prior to the advertised time for the opening of bids or proposals, excluding Saturdays, Sundays, and legal holidays, then the opening of bids or proposals shall be extended at least 72 hours, excluding Saturdays, Sundays, and legal holidays, from the date of the original bid or proposal opening without need to re-advertise. 
(e)  Any competitive sealed bidding process shall comply with the following requirements: 
(1)  The board of commissioners shall publicly advertise an invitation for bids; 
(2)  Bidders shall submit sealed bids based on the criteria set forth in such invitation; 
(3)  The board of commissioners shall open the bids publicly and evaluate such bids without discussion with the bidders; and 
(4)  The contract shall be awarded to the lowest responsible and responsive bidder whose bid meets the requirements and criteria set forth in the invitation for bids; provided, however, that if the bid from the lowest responsible and responsive bidder exceeds the funds budgeted for the public works construction contract, the board of commissioners may negotiate with such apparent low bidder to obtain a contract price within the budgeted amount. Such negotiations may include changes in the scope of work and other bid requirements. 
(f)  Any competitive sealed proposal shall comply with the following requirements: 
(1)  The board of commissioners shall publicly advertise a request for proposals, which request shall include conceptual program information in the request for proposals describing the requested services in a level of detail appropriate to the project delivery method selected for the project, as well as the relative importance of the evaluation factors; 
(2)  The board of commissioners shall open all proposals received at the time and place designated in the request for proposals so as to avoid disclosure of contents to competing offerors during the process of negotiations; and 
(3)  The board of commissioners shall make an award to the responsible and responsive offeror whose proposal is determined in writing to be the most advantageous to the county, taking into consideration the evaluation factors set forth in the request for proposals. The evaluation factors shall be the basis on which the award decision is made. The contract file shall indicate the basis on which the award is made. 
(4)  Discussions, negotiations, and revisions may be permitted after submission of proposals and prior to award for the purpose of obtaining best and final offers. In accordance with the request for proposals, all responsible offerors found by the board of commissioners to have submitted proposals reasonably susceptible of being selected for award shall be given an opportunity to participate in such discussions, negotiations, and revisions. During the process of discussion, negotiation, and revision, the board of commissioners shall not disclose the contents of proposals to competing offerors. 
(g)  Exceptions. 
(1)  The requirements of this section shall not apply to public works construction projects, when the same can be performed at a cost of less than $100,000.00. Public works construction projects shall not be subdivided in an effort to evade the provisions of this section. 
(2)  This section shall not apply in the event that the board of commissioners contracts with a governmental entity having a correctional institution for the use of inmate labor from such institution and use the inmates in the performance of any public works construction project. 
(3)  This section shall not apply in the event that the labor used or to be used in a public works construction project is furnished at no expense by the state or federal government or any agency thereof, and the board of commissioners shall have the power and authority to purchase material for such public works construction project and use the labor furnished free to the county. 
(4)  The requirements of this section shall not apply to public works construction projects necessitated by an emergency; provided, however, that the nature of the emergency shall be described in the minutes of the board of commissioners. Any contract let by the county pursuant to this subsection shall be ratified, as soon as practicable, on the minutes of the board of commissioners, and the nature of the emergency shall be described therein. 
(5)  The requirements of this section shall not apply to public works construction projects or any portion of a public works construction project self-performed by the board of commissioners. If the board of commissioners contracts with a private person or entity for a portion of such project, the provisions of this section shall apply to any such contract estimated to exceed $100,000.00. 
(6)  The requirements of this section shall not apply to sole source public works construction contracts. 
(h)  Bid bond requirements. 
(1)  Bid bonds shall be required for all public works construction contracts subject to the requirements of this subsection with estimated bids or proposals over $100,000.00. However, the board of commissioners may require a bid bond for projects with estimated bids or proposals of $100,000.00 or less. 
(2)  In the case of competitive sealed bids, a bid may not be revoked or withdrawn until 60 days after the time set by the board of commissioners for opening of bids. Upon expiration of this time period, the bid will cease to be valid, unless the bidder provides written notice to the board of commissioners prior to the scheduled expiration date that the bid will be extended for a time period specified by the board of commissioners. 
(3)  In the case of competitive sealed proposals, the board of commissioners shall advise offerors in the request for proposals of the number of days that offerors will be required to honor their proposals; provided, however, that if an offeror is not selected within 60 days of opening the proposals, any offeror that is determined by the board of commissioners to be unlikely of being selected for contract award shall be released from his or her proposal. 
(4)  If the board of commissioners requires a bid bond for any public works construction contract, no bid or proposal for a contract with the board of commissioners shall be valid for any purpose unless the contractor shall give a bid bond with good and sufficient surety or sureties approved by the board of commissioners. The bid bond shall be in the amount of not less than five percent of the total amount payable by the terms of the contract. 
(5)  In lieu of the bid bond provided for in this subsection, the board of commissioners may accept a cashier's check, or cash in the amount of not less than five percent of the total amount payable by the terms of the contract payable to and for the protection of the county. 
(6)  When the amount of any bid bond required under this subsection does not exceed $750,000.00, the board of commissioners may, in its sole discretion, accept an irrevocable letter of credit issued by a bank or savings and loan association in the amount and in lieu of the bond otherwise required. 
(i)  Withdrawal of bids for appreciable errors. 
(1)  As used in this subsection, the term bid includes proposal and the term bidder includes offeror. 
(2)  A bidder shall be permitted to withdraw a bid from consideration after the bid opening without forfeiture of the bid security if the bidder has made an appreciable error in the calculation of his or her bid and if: 
a.  Such error in the calculation of his or her bid can be documented by clear and convincing written evidence; 
b.  Such error can be clearly shown by objective evidence drawn from inspection of the original work papers, documents, or materials used in the preparation of the bid sought to be withdrawn; 
c.  The bidder serves written notice upon the board of commissioners prior to the award of the contract and not later than 48 hours after the opening of bids, excluding Saturdays, Sundays, and legal holidays; 
d.  The bid was submitted in good faith and the mistake was due to a calculation or clerical error, an inadvertent omission, or a typographical error as opposed to an error in judgment; and 
e.  The withdrawal of the bid will not result in undue prejudice to the governmental entity or other bidders by placing them in a materially worse position than they would have occupied if the bid had never been submitted. 
(3)  In the event that an apparent successful bidder has withdrawn his or her bid as provided in subsection (i)(2), action on the remaining bids should be considered as though the withdrawn bid had not been received. In the event the project is re-let for bids, under no circumstances shall a bidder who has filed a request to withdraw a bid be permitted to resubmit a bid for the work. 
(4)  No bidder who is permitted to withdraw a bid pursuant to subsection (i)(2) shall for compensation supply any material or labor to, or perform any subcontract or other work agreement for, the person or firm to whom the contract is awarded or otherwise benefit, directly or indirectly, from the performance of the project for which the withdrawn bid was submitted. 
(j)  Withdrawal of bid or proposals by affiliated corporation. 
(1)  Affiliated corporation means, with respect to any corporation, any other corporation related thereto: 
a.  As a parent corporation; 
b.  As a subsidiary corporation; 
c.  As a sister corporation; 
d.  By common ownership or control; or 
e.  By control of one corporation by the other. 
(2)  In any case where two or more affiliated corporations bid or propose for a contract under this subsection and any one or more of such affiliated corporations subsequently rescind or revoke their bid or proposal in favor of another such affiliated corporation whose bid or proposal is for a higher amount and the contract is awarded at such higher amount to such other affiliated corporation, then the bid bond, proposal guaranty, or other security otherwise required under this subsection of each affiliated corporation rescinding or revoking its bid or proposal shall be forfeited. 
(k)  Performance bond requirements.
