(1)  Performance bonds shall be required for all public works construction contracts subject to the requirements of this subsection with an estimated contract amount greater than $100,000.00; provided however, that the board of commissioners may require a performance bond for public works construction contracts that are estimated at $100,000.00 or less. No public works construction contract requiring a performance bond shall be valid for any purpose unless the contractor shall give such performance bond. The performance bond shall be in the amount of at least the total amount payable by the terms of the contract and shall be increased as the contract amount is increased. 
(2)  When the amount of the performance bond required under this subsection does not exceed $750,000.00, the board of commissioners may, in its sole discretion, accept an irrevocable letter of credit by a bank or savings and loan association in the amount of and in lieu of the bond otherwise required under this subsection. 
(l)  Requirement for payment bonds. Payment bonds shall be required for all public works construction contracts subject to the requirements of this subsection with an estimated contract amount greater than $100,000.00; provided, however, that the board of commissioners may require a payment bond for public works construction contracts that are estimated at $100,000.00 or less. No public works construction contract requiring a payment bond shall be valid for any purpose, unless the contractor shall give such payment bond; provided, however, that, in lieu of such payment bond, the board of commissioners, in its discretion, may accept a cashier's check, certified check, or cash for the use and protection of all subcontractors and all persons supplying labor, materials, machinery, and equipment in the prosecution of work provided in the contract. The payment bond or other security accepted in lieu of a payment bond shall be in the amount of at least the total amount payable by the terms of the initial contract and shall be increased if requested by the board of commissioners as the contract amount is increased. 
(Ord. of 10-26-1993, § XI; Amd. of 12-8-2009) 
Sec. 2-123. - Exceptions to competitive bidding. 
The board of commissioners and/or purchasing manager, as determined by the authority to award bids or quotations for contracts and/or purchases, shall be authorized to waive any and all bidding requirements for the purchase of necessary materials, supplies, equipment, or services under the following circumstances: 
(1)  Emergency purchases. An emergency purchase will be authorized when conditions exist which present a threat to the safety, health, and welfare of the citizens of the county and whenever such requirements would cause an undue delay in the delivery of essential county services under such conditions. Emergency purchases shall be made pursuant to the purchasing manual. If an emergency should arise after hours or on holidays, which requires immediate action on the part of the department involved for the protection and best interest of the county, or should a like situation arise on a weekend, and where it is not possible to reach the purchasing manager, any purchase necessary shall be made by the user agency's department head, and such purchase reported to the purchasing manager pursuant to the attached purchasing manual. 
(2)  Cooperative purchasing agreements. Cooperative purchasing agreements will be formed whenever, in the judgment of the board of commissioners and/or the purchasing manager, it would be in the best interest of the county to enter into cooperative purchasing agreements with other units of government. 
(3)  Federal and state contract purchases. Whenever any goods or services are available to the county through a contract with the federal or state government, and when such items or services meet the requirements of a user agency, such items or services shall be deemed to have met all requirements of competitive bidding and may be purchased under the federal or state contract without regard to further government requirements. 
(4)  Professional/contractual services. Professional/contractual services may not be subject to competitive bidding pursuant to section 2-120. 
(5)  Sole source purchases. The purchasing manager shall be authorized to designate a sole source for any item or service, the purchase of which, due to specific scientific technology or extraordinary specifications and circumstances, is available from only one vendor. Any such purchase shall be documented as to the reasons for the sole source and shall be maintained by the purchasing manager. 
(6)  Road paving purchases. The purchasing manager is authorized to approve purchases not to exceed $100,000.00 without advertisement or bids for road surfacing materials, such as gravel, asphalt, concrete and pipe, for any complete road surfacing or resurfacing project within the county. 
(7)  Election materials purchase. In circumstances where the state designates a particular vendor for the purchase of election materials, these items will be purchased with a county purchase order without regard to further requirements of this division, excluding budgetary constraints. 
(8)  Limited vendor purchases. In cases where available vendors for a given item or service to be purchased are outside the general circulation of the county's legal organ, the board of commissioners may waive the requirement to advertise the request for sealed bid. In all cases where the board waives the advertising requirement, a copy of the request for sealed bid will be posted in a prominent location within the courthouse and all known qualified vendors will be sent a request for sealed bid. 
(9)  Used equipment purchases. 
a.  In cases where Peach County is seeking opportunities to purchase used equipment, the user agency will write minimum specifications and requirements for the piece of equipment being sought. The purchasing manager will post the specifications with details on the time period that the search for suitable used equipment will be performed and sufficient information for prospective vendors holding used equipment meeting the specifications to respond to the posting and make the availability of their equipment known to the county. The posting will be placed in the courthouse at a location known to the public for such postings, on the county website, and emailed to vendors that have provided an email address. All vendor submissions will be evaluated by the user agency, with consideration being given to price, suitability, specifications, age, condition, and distance. 
b.  In cases where the county is seeking opportunities to purchase used equipment expected to cost at least $10,000.00, the purchasing manager will post the specifications with details on the time period that the search for suitable used equipment will be performed by formal advertisement in the legal organ of the county. Said advertisement shall run for two consecutive weeks. 
c.  Transactions between Peach County and any other governmental entity shall be exempt from the above stated policy. Peach County shall retain the right to purchase, transfer, donate, or sale [sell] any piece of used equipment with the Georgia Department of Administrative Services or with any other governmental entity. 
(Ord. of 10-26-1993, § XII; Ord. of 4-26-1994; Amd. of 12-8-2009; Mo. of 4-6-2010) 
Sec. 2-124. - Local preference. 
It shall be the policy of the county government to encourage, stimulate, and foster the expansion of existing business/industry and to encourage the location of new businesses/industries/industries in the community. 
(Ord. of 10-26-1993, § XIII) 
Sec. 2-125. - Authorized purchases. 
(a)  Except as otherwise provided herein and in the attached purchasing manual, all purchases for materials, supplies, and services for the county shall be on an official Peach County purchase order as prescribed in this division, issued by the purchasing manager or his designee, and in accordance with the procedures in the attached purchasing manual. 
(b)  No department head, public official, or employee shall commit to any vendor for the purchase of any supplies or services except those exemptions noted herein and in the attached purchasing manual. 
(c)  Except as otherwise provided for in this section, no purchase order shall be issued on behalf of the county unless there is a sufficient unencumbered fund balance, in excess of all unpaid obligations, of the user agency to cover the amount of such purchase. 
(d)  Any purchase made outside the provisions and procedures stated in this division and purchasing manual, to include the provisions for bona fide emergencies, will not be paid with county funds. These obligations will be incurred by the individual responsible for the purchase. 
(Ord. of 10-26-1993, § XIV; Amd. of 12-8-2009) 
Sec. 2-126. - Price agreement contracts. 
Goods or services used by one or more user agencies on a regular and continuing basis may be purchased under a contract covering a specified extended period of time, at an established price for such goods or services, which shall be valid for the duration of the contract period. Purchase agreements under this section shall be subject to applicable bidding or quotation requirements as any other purchase. 
(Ord. of 10-26-1993, § XV) 
Sec. 2-127. - Vendor in default. 
The purchasing manager shall not accept any bid or quotation from, nor issue any purchase order to, any vendor or contractor for any of the following reasons: 
(1)  The vendor is in default on the payment of any county taxes, license fee, or other monies due the county. 
(2)  The vendor is in default due to a declaration of ineligibility pursuant to section 2-114(5). 
(Ord. of 10-26-1993, § XVI; Amd. of 12-8-2009) 
Sec. 2-128. - Protest procedures. 
The following procedures and time requirements shall be applied uniformly in processing all protests pertaining to the contract solicitation process or contract award decision. 
(1)  Protests may be made by active or prospective bidders whose direct economic interest would be affected by a solicitation, proposed award, or award of a contract. 
(2)  Protests must be made in writing and be received within the timelines of this policy and should be concise, logically arranged, clearly state the grounds for the protest, and must include at least the following information. 
a.  Name, address, and telephone number of protestor. 
b.  Solicitation or contract name and/or number. 
c.  A detailed statement of the legal and factual grounds for the protest, including copies of all relevant documents or information. 
d.  A statement of relief requested. 
(3)  Upon receipt of a protest, the purchasing manager will notify the protestor by mail within five working days that the protest has been received. The purchasing manager may request additional information from the protesting party, which must be submitted in writing to the purchasing manager within five working days from the date of the purchasing manager's request. The purchasing manager will forward all documentation submitted by the protestor to the board of commissioners. 
(4)  Within 20 working days of receipt of a written protest, the board of commissioners shall either: 
a.  Issue a final written decision which responds in detail to each issue raised in the protest and includes a rationale for the decision rendered, or 
b.  Conduct, at the county's discretion, an informal hearing to allow the interested participating parties an opportunity to present their positions and supporting facts, documents, justification, and technical information. The county will advise all interested parties of the final decision in writing no later than five working days from the date of the informal hearing. 
(5)  The county's decision shall be final. A request to reconsider such decision will only be allowed if relevant data becomes available that was not previously known or if there has been an error of law or regulation. Such a request for reconsideration must be made within five working days after notification of the county's final decision. 
(6)  Protests before proposal solicitation. Bid protests alleging restrictive specifications or improprieties, which are apparent prior to bid or proposal opening, must be submitted in writing to the purchasing manager and must be received at least five working days prior to bid/proposal opening. If the written protest is not received by the time specified, bids or proposals may be received, opened, and awarded in the normal manner unless the county determines that it is in the best interest of all concerned to delay any step. Bids will not be opened until five working days after resolution of the protest unless the county determines that: 
a.  The items to be procured are urgently required; 
b.  Delivery or performance will be unduly delayed by failure to make award promptly; or 
c.  Failure to make award will otherwise cause undue harm to the county. 
(7)  Protests after opening of proposal solicitation and prior to award. Protests against the making of an award may be made after bid opening and prior to award. Such protests must be submitted in writing to the purchasing manager and must be received by the purchasing manager within five working days of the bid opening. If the county decides to withhold the award pending resolution of the protest, the county will notify all bidders whose bids or proposal might become eligible for award, and offer them the option to extend or withdraw their bid or proposal. Awards will not be made until at least five working days after resolution of the protest unless the county determines that: 
a.  The items to be procured are urgently required; 
b.  Delivery or performance will be unduly delayed by failure to make award promptly; or 
c.  Failure to make award will otherwise cause undue harm to the county. 
(8)  Protests after award. Protests received after announcement of an award or after a contract has been executed will only be considered if the county determines that the matter is in the public interest or the protest presents clear and convincing evidence of fraud, misrepresentation, other illegality, or gross impropriety in the selection of a proposal. If a protest is under consideration, the county shall evaluate the proposal at issue a second time in its entirety and use the same evaluation criteria and rating factors applied in the initial review of the proposal. The proposal will be evaluated by the board of commissioners. 
(9)  Protests after contract executed. If a protest involving an executed contract is under consideration, the county will notify the selected contractor of the protest and its basis and may, at its discretion, order the contractor to suspend all county work activities. If the awarded contractor has not executed the contract as of the date the protest is received by the county, the contract will not be executed until five working days after resolution of the protest unless the county determines that: 
a.  The items to be procured are urgently required; 
b.  Delivery or performance will be unduly delayed by failure to make award promptly; or 
c.  Failure to make award will otherwise cause undue harm to the county. 
(10)  Solicitations and awards for projects funded by the Federal Transit Administration. 
a.  The county shall, in all instances involving the solicitation and award of projects funded by the Federal Transit Administration, report any protest or dispute to the FTA within five working days from the date the protest is filed with the county. The county shall provide to the FTA within five working days following the county's decision on the protest, copies of all documents pursuant to the protest and a copy of the written decision pursuant to the protest. 
b.  A protestor may file an appeal with the Federal Transit Administration under certain limited circumstances where the bid solicitation and contract award is for a project that is being funded through the Federal Transit Administration (FTA), after the county has rendered a decision on a bid protest. FTA's review of any protest will be limited to an alleged failure by the county to have written protest procedures or alleged failure by the county to follow such procedures. 
c.  A protestor desiring to do so shall file its protest with FTA not later than five days after the final decision of the county is rendered under the county's protest procedure. In instances where the protestor alleges that the county failed to make a final determination on the protest, the protestor shall file a complaint with FTA no later than five days after the protestor knew or should have known of the county's failure to render a final determination on the protest. 
d.  Protests to FTA should be filed with the appropriate FTA Regional Office with a concurrent copy to the county. The protest filed with FTA shall be filed in accordance with FTA Circular 4220.1E, include the name and address of the protestor, identify the county project number, contain a statement of the grounds for the protest and any supporting documentation, and include a copy of the local protest filed with the county and a copy of the county's decision, if any. 
e.  The submission of unsolicited proposals for FTA contract funds is inconsistent with county policy to promote a full and open competition among interested parties. The filing of unsolicited proposals for FTA contract funds, therefore, will be deemed inappropriate by the county and returned to the sender, and complaints or appeals calling for reconsideration of such proposals will not be accepted. 
(Amd. of 12-8-2009) 
Secs. 2-129—2-138. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - INVESTMENT POLICY[9] 

Footnotes: 
--- (9) --- 
Editor's note— Ord. of 11-13-2007, was renumbered for classification purposes at the editor's discretion. The provisions have been included as §§ 2-139—2-153. See also the Code Comparative Table. 

Sec. 2-139. - Intent. 
It is the intent of the Peach County Board of Commissioners to establish regulations and procedures to provide for an efficient and fiscally responsible investment management program, to diversify investment portfolios by maturity date, to structure investment portfolios to meet all anticipated net outflows that are projected to occur, and to ensure that the administration of such a program is in accordance with the highest ethical and fiscal standards and applicable laws. 
(Ord. of 11-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-140. - Applicability. 
(a)  This policy governs the investment of the "General Fund Investment Portfolio," which includes the General Fund. 
(b)  This policy governs the investment of the "Special Revenue Fund Portfolio," which encompasses enterprise funds and special revenue funds, as follows: 
(1)  Solid Waste Management Enterprise Fund; 
(2)  Special Purpose Local Option Sales Tax Funds; 
(3)  E911 Fund; 
(4)  Hotel/Motel Fund; 
(5)  Transit Fund; 
(c)  This policy does not govern the General Employee's Pension Fund. 
(Ord. of 11-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-141. - Objective. 
Investment of the funds covered by this policy shall be governed by the following investment objectives: 
(a)  Legality. All investments shall fully comply with federal, state, and local laws. Additional requirements are discussed in the authorized and suitable investment section of this investment policy. 
(b)  Safety. Safety of principal is the primary objective of the investment policy. Investment of the county funds shall be undertaken in a manner that seeks to ensure the preservation of capital for the overall portfolio. 
(c)  Liquidity. The county's investment portfolio will remain sufficiently liquid to enable the county to meet all operating requirements that might be reasonably anticipated. 
(d)  Yield. The county's investment portfolio shall be designed with the objective of attaining a market rate of return, throughout budgetary and economic cycles, while taking into consideration the investment risk constraints and cash flow characteristics of the portfolio. 
(Ord. of 11-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-142. - Delegation of authority. 
The Peach County Board of Commissioners shall assume ultimate responsibility regarding investment decisions on behalf of the county. The board of commissioners designates the county administrator to approve the bidding and/or re-bidding of due investments and new investments. Under the provisions of state and county codes, the county administrator has the ability to designate an employee of the finance division to manage the daily investments of county funds. This responsibility has been designated to the accounting manager who assumes the day-to-day investment management. 
(Ord. of 11-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-143. - Controls and procedures. 
(a)  The county administrator or his/her designee shall establish written procedures for the operation of the investment program consistent with this investment policy. Such procedures shall include explicit delegation of authority to any other persons responsible for investment transactions. No person may engage in an investment transaction except as provided under the terms of this policy and the written procedures. Authority granted to a person to invest the county's funds is effective until rescinded or until termination of the person's employment by the county. The county administrator shall be responsible for all transactions undertaken and shall establish a system of controls, to be reviewed by the county auditor, to regulate the activities of subordinate officials. Both the county administrator and the accounting manager shall possess sufficient working knowledge of economics and securities markets, as well as the supervisory experience and judgment necessary to carry out the responsibilities outlined in this policy. 
(b)  Formal written procedures shall also include but not be limited to: 
(1)  A formal process that outlines procedures relating to the purchase and sale of securities. 
(2)  A formal reporting system to monitor the performance of investment securities held. This system shall include written reports as outlined in sections 3-123 and 3-124 of this policy. 
(3)  A system of compliance with generally accepted accounting principles (GAAP) of the Government Accounting Standards Board. 
(4)  A system of internal controls, designed to detect errors, misrepresentation or imprudent actions. 
(5)  Thorough cross training of department employees to allow for back up of critical investment duties. 
(6)  An annual review of investment operations by the county's auditors. 
(Ord. of 11-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-144. - Prudence. 
The accounting manager shall adhere to the "prudent investor" standard as suggested by the Government Finance Officers Association (GFOA), which states that: "Investments shall be made with judgment and care, under circumstances then prevailing, which persons of prudence, discretion and intelligence exercise in the management of their own affairs, not for speculation, but for investment, considering the probable safety of their capital as well as the probable income to be derived." 
(a)  The "prudent investor" standard shall be applied in the context of managing an overall portfolio. Investment officers who exercise due diligence and act in accordance with the investment policy and written procedures, shall be relieved of personal responsibility for an individual security's credit risk or market price changes, provided deviations from expectations are reported in a timely fashion and appropriate action is taken to control adverse developments. 
(b)  Accounting manager, while acting in accordance with this policy and written procedures pertaining to the administration and management of the county's assets, and who exercises proper due diligence, shall be relieved of personal responsibility for an individual security's credit risk or market price changes, provided that deviations from expectations are reported in a timely fashion and appropriate action is taken to control and prevent any further adverse developments. 
(c)  Securities shall not be purchased with trading or speculation as the dominant selection criteria. 
(Ord. of 11-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-145. - Ethics and conflicts of interest. 
Officers and employees involved in the investment process shall refrain from personal business activity that could conflict with proper execution of the investment program, or which could impair their ability to make impartial investment decisions. 
(a)  Officers and employees involved in the investment process shall disclose any material interests in financial institutions with which they conduct business. 
(b)  Officers and employees involved in the investment process shall disclose any large personal financial/investment positions that could be related to the performance of the investment portfolio. The county's statute on conflict of interest and disclosure shall be strictly followed. 
(Ord. of 11-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-146. - Authorized and suitable investments. 
(a)  Instruments rated below an AAA rating may not be purchased. However, investments in instruments other than government securities shall be made only if the yield is equal to or greater than the bond equivalent yield on U.S. Treasury obligations of comparable maturity. County funds governed by this policy may be invested in the instruments described below. 
(1)  Obligations of the State of Georgia or of other states; 
(2)  The local government investment pool established by O.C.G.A. § 36-83-8; 
(3)  Obligations issued by the United States government; 
(4)  Obligations fully insured or guaranteed by the United States government or a United States government agency: 
a.  Federal Farm Credit System; 
b.  Federal Home Loan Bank System; 
c.  Federal Home Loan Mortgage Corporation; 
d.  Federal National Mortgage Association; 
e.  Student Loan Marketing Association; 
f.  Federal Agricultural Mortgage Corporation. 
(b)  Purchase of non-negotiable certificates of deposit. 
(c)  Investments not listed, including options and reverse repurchase agreements, are strictly prohibited. In addition, the board of commissioners may at times restrict or prohibit the purchase of specific issues due to current market conditions. 
(d)  No public deposit shall be made except in a qualified public depository as established by state law. 
(Ord. of 11-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-147. - Competitive bidding. 
(a)  It is the policy of the county to limit investment transactions to those banks and broker/dealers on the Peach County's approved bid list. In addition, the county shall seek three competitive bids and offers on all individual security purchases and sales. 
(b)  All bids and offers received shall be documented and retained. It shall be the responsibility of the accounting manager associated with the transaction to record the following minimum information: 
(1)  Financial institution selected; 
(2)  Rate quoted; 
(3)  Security description; 
(4)  Cover bids/offers; 
(5)  Special considerations in the event that the lowest priced security was not selected. 
(Ord. of 11-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-148. - Collateralization. 
(a)  The county requires that all investments plus accrued interest, if any, in depository accounts be secured in accordance with this policy. 
(b)  Collateral will always be held by an independent third party and shall be reviewed at least monthly to ensure that the market value of the pledged securities is adequate. 
(1)  Securities authorized for collateral under this policy are limited to those investments outlined in section 3-118 (a)(1-4), (b). 
(2)  The collateralization level for certificates of deposit shall be 110 percent of the market value of principal and accrued interest. 
(Ord. of 11-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-149. - Safekeeping and custody. 
Safekeeping and custody of securities and collateral shall be in accordance with state law. All securities transactions, except local government investment pool and money market mutual fund transactions shall be conducted on a delivery versus payment (DVP) basis. Securities and collateral will be held by a third party custodian, and shall be held in the county's name as evidenced by original safekeeping receipts of the institution with which the securities are deposited. The custodian shall also provide monthly safekeeping statements that contain sufficient detail of securities held including, but not limited to, par, security type, CUSIP, maturity date, coupon and market value. 
(Ord. of 11-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-150. - Diversification and maximum maturities. 
The county shall seek to ladder the maturities of the portfolio to correspond with known projected cash flow needs, taking into consideration large reoccurring expenditure items such as payroll and bond disbursements. The county shall seek to maintain a weighted-average maturity of the total portfolio not to exceed one year. 
(Ord. of 11-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-151. - Portfolio monitoring. 
All trading losses incurred shall be reported immediately to the county administrator with appropriate documentation that formed the basis for the transaction. A summary of trading gains and losses shall be provided to the county administrator not less than on a monthly basis in order to determine the propriety of trading activity. 
(Ord. of 11-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-152. - Reporting. 
The accounting manager shall prepare a monthly investment report. This report, which will include a summary of the current status of the general investment portfolio and security transactions made over the prior month, will be provided to the Peach County Board of Commissioners. The report as a minimum should include: 
(a)  Detail of portfolio holdings and interest earned; 
(b)  Maturity dates; 
(c)  A budget comparison. 
(Ord. of 11-13-2007) 
Sec. 2-153. - Investment strategies. 
(a)  The following strategies may be used to maximize return on investments: 
(1)  Matching maturities to anticipated cash flow requirements; 
(2)  Anticipating market changes. 
(b)  Although it is not possible to consistently predict market trends, an understanding of the factors that affect the market is important when determining an optimal maturity for the portfolio. Trading is not to be made solely on the basis of interest rate forecasts, but specific decisions involving maturity dates should consider short-term market expectations. 
(Ord. of 11-13-2007) 
Secs. 2-154—2-180. - Reserved. 
DIVSION 4. - PURCHASING CARD AND CREDIT CARD FOR PEACH COUNTY ELECTED OFFICIALS[10] 

Footnotes: 
--- (10) --- 
Editor's note— An ordinance adopted Dec. 8, 2015, §§ I—VII, did not specifically amend the Code; hence, inclusion as Div. 4, §§ 2-181—2-187, was at the discretion of the editor. 

Sec. 2-181. - Intent and scope. 
This division is intended to comply with the policy requirements of O.C.G.A. § 36-80-24 regarding the use of county issued government purchasing cards and credit cards. 
(Ord. No. 12-8-2015, § I) 
Sec. 2-182. - Definitions. 
[The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:] 
Authorized elected official means an elected official designated by public vote of the board of commissioners to receive a county issued government purchasing card or credit card. 
Card administrator means the purchasing card and credit card administrator designated by the Peach County Board of Commissioners. 
County means Peach County and/or the board of commissioners. 
County purchase card , county p-card or county credit card means a financial transaction card issued by any business organization, financial institution, or any duly authorized agent of such organization or institution, used by a county official to purchase gods, services and other things of value on behalf of the county. 
Financial transaction card means an instrument or device as the term is defined in O.C.G.A. § 16-9-30(5). 
User agreement means the required agreement between the board of commissioners and the authorized elected officials which restricts the use of a county purchasing card or credit card. 
(Ord. of 12-8-2015, § II) 
Sec. 2-183. - Designated elected officials. 
The Peach County Board of Commissioners ("county"), in its discretion, may authorize specific county elected officials to use a county purchasing card or credit card by adoption of a resolution in a public meeting. 
No authorized elected official may use a county purchasing card or credit card until and unless he or she has executed the county's purchasing card and credit card user agreement. 
The county will not make payments to any business organization, financial institution, or any duly authorized agent of such organization or institution, for amounts charged by an elected official to any purchasing cards or credit cards that are not issued pursuant to this division or for any purchases that are not authorized by this division. 
(Ord. of 12-8-2015, § III) 
Sec. 2-184. - Card administrator. 
The board of commissioners shall designate a county purchasing card and credit card administrator. The responsibilities of the card administrator include: 
(1)  Manage county issued purchasing cards and credit cards. 
(2)  Serve as the main point of contact for all county purchasing card and credit card issues. 
(3)  Serve as liaison to the elected officials authorized to use a purchasing card or credit card and their staff, as well as to the issuer of the purchasing card or credit card. 
(4)  Provide training on card policies and procedures to the elected officials authorized to use a purchasing card or credit card and their staff. 
(5)  Develop internal procedures to ensure timely payment of cards. 
(6)  Assist authorized elected officials to dispute transactions when necessary. 
(7)  Establish internal procedures to ensure compliance with this division, county procurement ordinances and policies, county purchasing card and credit card user agreements, applicable agreements with the business organization, financial institution, or any duly authorized agent of such organization or institution, issuing card, and state law, specifically, O.C.G.A. §§ 16-9-37 and 36-80-24. 
(8)  Document internal controls, audits and other measures to prevent and detect misuse or abuse of the cards. 
(9)  Audit and reconcile transactions monthly. 
(10)  Maintain records for at least seven years or as otherwise provided by the county's record retention policy. 
(Ord. of 12-8-2015, § IV) 
Sec. 2-185. - Use of cards. 
(a)  Authorized purchases . County purchase cards and credit cards may be used to purchase goods and services directly related to the public duties of the authorized elected official only. All purchases are subject to the terms of this division, the county purchasing card and credit card user agreement, county procurement policies and ordinances, and the adopted budget. 
Only authorized elected officials may use a county purchase card or credit card for purchases or payments. The cards, and use of the cards, are not transferrable to employees. The authorized elected official shall use care to ensure that others do not have access to the card account number, expiration date and security code. 
The board of commissioners, at its sole discretion, may provide a credit card and/or purchasing card to select elected officials on a non-temporary basis, and said elected official shall: 
(1)  Ensure that the use of each card is accounted for on forms provided by the finance department; 
(2)  Ensure that each card is secured when not in use; 
(3)  Designate which subordinates, if any, are authorized to use the credit card and/or purchasing card and provide said authorization listing to card administrator; 
(4)  Ensure that sufficient purchase documentation and corresponding receipts are provided to the finance department in a timely manner to ensure that each billing statement is reconciled monthly; 
(5)  Ensure that any billing discrepancies are resolved with the vendor; 
(6)  Document any unauthorized use of the credit card and/or purchasing card and report same to the card administrator; 
(7)  Document any vendor disputes related to the credit card and/or purchasing card and report same to the card administrator on at least a monthly basis; and 
(8)  Notify the card administrator immediately upon learning that a credit card and/or purchasing card is lost or stolen. 
Unless otherwise approved by the governing authority or established in the county purchasing card and credit card user agreement, the transaction limits are as follows: 
Per transaction: $2,500.00 
Per budget year: Not to exceed approved budget appropriation 
(b)  Unauthorized purchases . County purchasing cards and credit cards shall not be used for goods and services not directly related to the official responsibilities of the authorized elected official. Additionally, cards shall not be used to avoid compliance with the county's purchasing ordinances and procedures, to purchase goods and services that are not approved in the county's budget, to purchase goods and services exceeding the per transaction or per month limit, or to make purchases not in compliance with the county purchasing card and credit card user agreement. 
(c)  Receipts and documentation . Receipts, invoices and other supporting documentation of all purchases made with a county purchasing card or credit card shall be obtained and maintained by the authorized county elected official for five years or as otherwise provided by the county's record retention policy. If an original or duplicate cannot be produced, a sworn affidavit of the authorized elected official may be substituted. The documentation must include the supplier or merchant information (i.e., name and location), quantity, description, unit price, total price, price paid without sales tax and an explanation of the purchase sufficient to show that the expense was in the performance of official county duties. 
(d)  Public records . All receipt and other documentation of purchases are public records and subject to the requirements of O.C.G.A. § 50-18-70 et seq. 
(Ord. of 12-8-2015, § V) 
Sec. 2-186. - Review of purchases and audit. 
Proper documentation of purchases, internal controls and other measures prevent and allow detection to misuse or abuse of county issued purchase cards and credit cards. Authorized elected officials and staff that process payments under this program shall cooperate and comply with the procedures established by the county. 
(1)  Review of purchases . All purchases shall be reviewed according to the following procedure: 
(a)  The card administrator will be responsible for the issue of a county credit card or purchasing card and will record said issuance on a "cardholder approval and acknowledgement form." Each Peach County Elected Official will be required to sign the acknowledgement form upon receipt of the card. 
(b)  The Peach County Elected Official will provide the date, time, purpose, vendor name (if known), amount (if known) and general ledger account number(s) for the purchases to be made with the credit card or purchasing card. 
(c)  The Peach County Elected Official will promptly [within two business days] return all county credit cards and purchasing cards to the card administrator following the completion of the official county business or purchase for which the card was applied. All paperwork documenting the purchase will be returned to the card administrator with the card. 
(d)  The Peach County Elected Official will complete all required purchasing procedures as dictated in the Peach County Purchasing Ordinance pursuant to the credit card or purchasing card transaction. 
(2)  Audits . The card administrator shall perform an annual review of the card program to ensure adequacy of internal policies and procedures, cardholder spending limits, monthly reconciliation procedures and documentation for transactions. Elected officials and staff shall cooperate with such review. 
(Ord. of 12-8-2015, § VI) 
Sec. 2-187. - Violations. 
(a)  An elected official shall reimburse the county for any purchases made with a county issued purchase card or credit card in violation of this division or the user agreement. 
(b)  In the discretion of the county governing authority, failure to comply with the procedures outlined in this division may result in: 
(1)  A warning; 
(2)  Suspension of the elected official's authority to use a county purchase card or credit card; or 
(3)  Revocation of the elected official's authority to use a county-issued purchase card or credit card. 
(c)  Nothing in this division shall preclude the county governing authority from referring misuse of a purchase card or credit card for prosecution to the appropriate authorities. 
(Ord. of 12-8-2015, § VII) 
Chapter 6 - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Amusements and entertainments, ch. 8; alcoholic beverages at adult entertainment establishments, § 8-35; businesses, ch. 18. 
State Law reference— Use of proceeds of alcoholic beverage tax for prevention, education and treatment, Ga. Const. art. 3, sec. 9, par. 6(c); Georgia Alcoholic Beverage Code, O.C.G.A. § 3-1-1 et seq.; public drunkenness, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-41; furnishing alcoholic beverages to persons under 21 years of age, jurisdiction of municipal courts, O.C.G.A. § 36-32-10; treatment of alcoholics and intoxicated persons, O.C.G.A. § 37-8-1 et seq.; driving under the influence of alcohol or drugs, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-391. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 6-1—6-19. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - SALE AND DISTRIBUTION OF MALT BEVERAGES AND WINE[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Editor's note— Provisions enacted by an ordinance adopted Sept. 12, 1995, have been included herein at the discretion of the editor as Art. II, §§ 6-20—6-41. Formerly, § 6-1 saved from repeal the alcoholic beverage ordinance adopted May 29, 1973. 

Sec. 6-20. - Application. 
The following rules, requirements, licenses and standards shall be effective from September 12, 1995, and shall remain in effect until amended and/or modified thereafter. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95) 
Sec. 6-21. - Definitions. 
As used in this article: 
Governing authority means the Board of Commissioners of Peach County. 
Licensee means the person whose name appears upon a retail dealer's license and shall include the business entity operating pursuant thereto. 
Licensed premises means the business location of a licensed retail dealer existing on a single contiguous tract of real estate and operating under one name. 
Malt beverage means any alcoholic beverage obtained by the fermentation of any infusion or decoction of barley, malt, hops, or any other similar product, or any combination of such products in water, containing not more than six percent alcohol by volume, and including ale, porter, brown, stout, lager beer, malt beer, and strong beer, but not including sake, known as Japanese rice wine. 
Package means a bottle, can, keg, barrel, or other original consumer container. 
Person means any individual, firm, partnership, cooperative, non-profit membership corporation, joint venture, association, company, corporation, agency, syndicate, estate, trust, business trust, receiver, fiduciary, or other group or combination acting as a unit, body politic, or political subdivision, whether public, private, or quasi-public. 
Retail dealer means any person who sells malt beverages or wine, either in unbroken packages or for consumption on the premises, at retail only to consumers and not for resale. 
Retail dealer's license or license means a license to sell malt beverages or wine at retail either in unbroken packages or for consumption on the premises, issued by the governing authority pursuant to and subject to the terms of this article. 
Wine means any alcoholic beverage containing not more than 21 percent alcohol by volume made from fruits, berries, or grapes either by natural fermentation or by natural fermentation with brandy added. The term "wine" does not include cooking wine mixed with salt or other ingredients so as to render it unfit for human consumption as a beverage. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95, § 1; Mo. of 11-14-95; Ord. of 9-10-96) 
State Law reference— Similiar provisions, O.G.C.A. 3-1-2. 
Sec. 6-22. - Construction of definitions. 
As used in this article, defined words shall have the meanings specified unless the context in which the word or term is used clearly requires that a different meaning be used. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95, § 2) 
Sec. 6-23. - Retail dealer licenses; applications; notice; fingerprints; bonds; restrictions; standards; hearing. 
(a)  No malt beverages or wine shall be sold in Peach County except as authorized by a retail dealer's license issued pursuant to this article. Licenses issued hereunder shall authorize the sale of malt beverages and wine, as defined herein, only. Separate licenses are required for the sale of malt beverages and for the sale of wine. 
(b)  Application for a retail dealer's license shall be made on forms furnished by the governing authority. A notice of each application shall be advertised in the official gazette of Peach County, Georgia once a week for two weeks immediately preceding the meeting of the governing authority in which the application is to be acted upon. 
(c)  Each applicant shall furnish a complete set of fingerprints which shall be forwarded to the Peach County Sheriff's Department who shall search the files of the Georgia Crime Information Center for a period of five years immediately preceding the date of such application for any instance of criminal activity. The Peach County Sheriff's Department shall also submit such fingerprints to the Federal Bureau of Investigation under rules established by the United States Department of Justice for processing and identification records. The federal record, if any, shall be obtained and returned to the governing authority considering such application. 
Where it appears to the governing authority that an application is complete except for the F.B.I. fingerprint report, and that the applicant otherwise qualifies for a retail dealer's license, the governing authority may grant the license contingent on receiving a satisfactory F.B.I. report. Should the report provide grounds for denying the license, the license may be revoked immediately as though the application had been denied, and the licensee shall have the right to a hearing. 
(d)  Along with their application, applicants must post with the governing authority a personal performance bond, said bond to be conditioned upon the faithful observance and performance by the licensee of the rules and regulations contained in this article. Upon the violation of this article, or any part thereof, the amount of the bond to be forfeited will be determined by the governing authority in accordance with the nature of the violation after a hearing is held by the said governing authority. Written notice of such hearing shall be given to the alleged violator not less than 15 days prior thereto. The determination by the governing authority to forfeit such bond may be in addition to any action taken by the governing authority under section 6-40. Said bond shall be payable to Peach County, Georgia in the amount of $1,000.00, said bond to be approved by the governing authority and shall be executed in the form specified by the governing authority. However, nothing herein shall preclude the governing authority from waiving said bond requirement whenever a licensee has established sufficient financial responsibility and/or a record of faithful compliance with the laws and regulations of the United States of America, the State of Georgia and the County of Peach. 
(e)  No retail dealer's license shall be granted to any person or corporation unless such person is of legal age and such person or corporation is a resident of Peach County, Georgia or has its principal place of business located in peach County, Georgia. 
(f)  No employee of Peach County, Georgia shall be eligible to receive a retail dealer's license. 
(g)  The following standards shall be applied to all decisions pertaining to the issuance or denial of licenses hereunder: 
(1)  All applicants for a retail dealer's license must show financial responsibility. The governing authority may require all applicants to provide financial statements and other evidence of financial responsibility in conjunction with the application. 
(2)  All applicants for a retail dealer's license must be of good character, and all operators, managers, clerks, or other employees shall be of like character. Corporate or firm applicants shall be of good business reputation. 
(3)  No license shall be granted to an applicant who has been convicted under any federal, state, or local law for a criminal offense involving alcoholic beverages, gambling, or tax law violations if such conviction tends to indicate that the applicant would not maintain the operation for which a license is being sought in conformity with Federal, State or the laws of Peach County, Georgia. Furthermore, no license shall be granted if any operators, managers, clerks, or other employees employed by the applicant has been convicted under any Federal, State, or local law for a criminal offense involving alcoholic beverages, gambling, or tax law violations if such conviction tends to indicate that the applicant would not maintain the operation for which a license is being sought in conformity with Federal, State or the laws of Peach County, Georgia. 
(4)  A license application may be denied to any applicant for a retail dealer's license where it appears that the applicant would not have adequate financial participation in the proposed business to direct and manage its affairs, or where it appears that the applicant is intended to be a mere surrogate for a person or persons who would not otherwise qualify for a license for any reason whatsoever. 
(5)  The governing authority, in their discretion, may consider any extenuating circumstances which may reflect favorably or unfavorably on the applicant, application or the proposed location of the business. If, in the governing authority's sole judgment, circumstances are such that the granting of the license would not be in the best interest of the general public, such circumstances may be grounds for denying the application. 
(h)  All decisions of the governing authority either approving or denying a license application shall be stated in writing and a copy of such statement shall be provided to the applicant either personally or by certified mail within ten days of the decision. 
(i)  Whenever the governing authority shall deny an application for a retail dealer's license, the applicant shall have 15 days following notification of denial to request a hearing before the governing authority. The applicant shall be entitled to present evidence and cross-examine opposing witnesses at such hearing either with or without legal counsel. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95, § 3; Ord. of 4-6-96; Ord. of 9-10-96; Mo. of 11-6-96; Ord. of 8-12-14) 
Sec. 6-24. - Premises. 
No retail dealer's license shall be issued to any person unless the building in which the business will be located is complete and detailed plans of said building and outside premises are attached to the application, or unless proposed plans and specifications and a building permit for a building to be built or renovated are attached to the application. The completed building or the proposed building shall comply with ordinances of Peach County, Georgia, regulations of the State Revenue Commissioner and the laws of the State of Georgia. The proposed building shall also be subject to final inspection and approval when completed by the Building Inspector for Peach County. Each such building shall contain sufficient lighting so that the building itself and the premises on all sides of the building are readily visible at all times from the street on which the building is located so as to reveal the inside retail area of the building and so as to reveal all of the outside premises of said building. Each applicant for a retail dealer's license shall attach to his application evidence of ownership of the building or proposed building or a copy of the lease if the applicant is leasing the building. A separate retail dealer's license shall be required for each place of business. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95, § 4) 
Sec. 6-25. - Distance requirements. 
No retail dealer's license shall be granted to any person unless the entire business premises of the proposed location, including parking lot, is situated not less than 100 yards from any church building, not less than 200 yards from the property line of any school ground or college campus, and not less than 100 yards from any building used as an alcohol rehabilitation center, the same to be measured by the most direct route of travel on the ground. Each application for a retail dealer's license shall include a scale drawing of the location of the proposed premises showing the distance to the nearest church building, school ground or campus, or alcohol rehabilitation center, or a certificate of a registered surveyor that such location complies with this article with reference to this section. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95, § 5) 
Sec. 6-26. - Term of license; renewal. 
A retail dealer's license shall be valid only for the 12-month period from the date of issuance and no license may be renewed except upon approval of the governing authority. A licensee who desires to continue to operate during a subsequent year must apply for renewal prior to the expiration of his or her current license. An application for renewal is subject to the requirements of §§ 6-44—6-46. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95, § 6; Ord. of 9-10-96) 
Sec. 6-27. - License fees. 
The fee for each retail dealer's license shall be (as established by the county commission) per annum and shall be paid prior to the issuance of such license, said fee to accompany the application, and shall be either a bank certified check or money order. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95, § 7; Mo. of 11-6-96; Ord. of 8-12-14) 
Sec. 6-28. - Place of sale or delivery of goods. 
(a)  No licensee shall sell or deliver any malt beverages or wine to any person except in the licensed premises except as exempted under paragraph (b) of this section. A licensee shall be permitted to load only unopened packaged malt beverages and wine into a customer's vehicle when the sale physically takes place and monies have been exchanged inside the licensed premises. A licensee hereunder shall be permitted to have a drive-in window and it shall be permissible for the licensee to deliver unopened packaged malt beverages and wines through such window. "Curb service" type sales and sales to customers in vehicles parked in the parking area of licensed premises are prohibited. All other sales shall be for consumption on the licenses premises only. 
(b)  Open area sales and outdoor special events. 
(1)  Malt beverage and wine sales can be made by a licensed consumption on-premises establishment in an open area type environment or by a licensed caterer with a catering off-premises license at an outdoor special event if the establishment or event has been approved by the county marshal. 
(2)  The open area must be enclosed by some structure providing for public ingress/egress only through the main licensed premises. 
a.  The height of such structure shall be a minimum of four feet above the floor or ground. It must be approved by the county building inspector and the county fire department as required by governing regulations and codes. 
b.  The only exit from the area is to be through the licensed establishment's main premises and through an approved fire exit. 
(3)  An outdoor special event must be enclosed by some structure or fencing providing for public ingress/egress only through designated entrances and exits. 
a.  The outdoor special event must be approved by the county marshal and the Peach County Sheriff on crowd control, traffic, and security measures. 
b.  The event location must be properly zoned and approved by the Peach County Zoning Department. 
(c)  Promotion and sales. 
(1)  No licensee or employee or agent of a licensee, in connection with the sale or other disposition of malt beverages and wine for consumption on the premises shall: 
a.  Offer or deliver any free malt beverage or wine to any person or group of persons; however, nothing herein shall prohibit a brewery, winery, or distillery from distributing free samples in accordance with state law provisions; 
b.  Deliver more than one malt beverage or wine to one person at a time; however, nothing herein shall prohibit a brew pub from offering a sampler of malt beverages in containers not exceeding four ounces. Each sampler shall not exceed four different types of beverages. 
c.  The county marshal and the sheriff shall have responsibility for the enforcement of this article. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95, § 8; Ord. of 9-10-96; Ord. of 8-12-14) 
Sec. 6-29. - Hours of operation. 
No person, knowingly and intentionally, shall sell or offer to sell malt beverages and wine on: 
(1)  Sundays except between the hours of 12:30 p.m. and 11:30 p.m.; or 
(2)  Election days. Pursuant to the provisions of O.C.G.A. § 3-3-20, the sale of distilled spirits for consumption on the premises shall be permitted on election days as the same are defined in the Official Code of Georgia Annotated; provided, however, that it shall nonetheless be unlawful for any person to sell distilled spirits for consumption on the premises within 250 feet of any polling place or of the outer edge of any building within which such polling place is established on primary or election days. 
(3)  Christmas Day. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95, § 9; Mo. of 11-14-95; Ord. of 9-10-96; Mo. of 12-10-96; Ord. of 8-12-14) 
Sec. 6-30. - Minimum age of consumption; exceptions. 
(a)  No retail dealer or employee of a retail dealer shall knowingly furnish, sell or offer for sale any malt beverages or wine to a person prohibited to purchase malt beverages or wine under state law. This prohibition shall not apply with respect to the sale of malt beverages or wine to a person when such person has furnished proper identification showing that the person to whom the malt beverages or wine are being sold is 21 years of age or older. 
(b)  The above prohibition shall not apply with respect to the following: 
(1)  Whenever malt beverages or wine are purchased for medical purposes pursuant to a prescription of a physician duly authorized to practice medicine in this state; 
(2)  Whenever malt beverages or wine are purchased for consumption at a religious ceremony; or 
(3)  Whenever malt beverages or wine are possessed for consumption by a person under 21 years of age when the parent or guardian of the person under 21 years of age gives the alcoholic beverage to the person and when possession is in the home of the parent or guardian and such parent or guardian is present. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95, § 10; Mo. of 11-14-95; Ord. of 8-12-14) 
Sec. 6-31. - Employment of minors prohibited. 
No licensee shall employ, require, or permit a person under 21 years of age to sell or take orders for any malt beverage or wine. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95, § 11; Ord. of 9-10-96) 
Sec. 6-32. - Furnishing malt beverages or wine to certain persons prohibited. 
No licensee shall furnish, sell, or offer to sell any malt beverages or wine to any person who the licensee knows or reasonably should know is intoxicated, or is of unsound mind, or is a habitual drunkard. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95, § 12; Ord. of 9-10-96) 
Sec. 6-33. - Retail dealers to buy only from licensed wholesalers. 
No licensee shall buy or arrange to buy or in any way effect the transfer of any malt beverages or wine except from a licensed wholesaler. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95, § 13; Ord. of 9-10-96) 
Sec. 6-34. - Retail dealers to store inventory only on premises. 
A licensee shall keep no inventory or stock of malt beverages or wine at any place except the licensed premises, and within the licensed premises the storage area for malt beverages or wine shall be immediately adjacent to the retail area. No licensee shall enter into any type of arrangement whereby malt beverages or wine ordered by the licensee are stored by a licensed wholesaler. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95, § 14; Ord. of 9-10-96) 
Sec. 6-35. - Licenses not transferable. 
No retail dealer's license issued hereunder shall be transferable or assignable to any other person or location, and in the event that a licensed business is sold or closed, it shall be the duty of the licensee to immediately surrender the license to the governing authority. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95, § 15; Ord. of 9-10-96) 
Sec. 6-36. - Display of license. 
Licenses issued under this article shall be displayed prominently at all times on the premises for which same was issued. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95, § 16; Ord. of 9-10-96) 
Sec. 6-37. - Licensees to maintain a copy of the article; employees to be familiar with terms; responsibility of licensee for violations. 
Each licensee shall keep a copy of this article in the licensed premises and shall instruct any person working there with respect to the terms hereof and each licensee and the licensee's agents and employees selling malt beverages or wine shall at all times be familiar with the terms hereof. The acts of any person working in the licensed premises which occur on the licensed premises and are in violation of this article or of any federal, state or local law relating to the sale, regulation or control of alcoholic beverages or to drugs or gambling shall be attributable to the licensee for the purposes of enforcement of this article. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95, § 17; Ord. of 9-10-96) 
Sec. 6-38. - Premises open for inspection. 
The licensed premises shall be open to inspection at any and all times by officers or officials representing the governing authority authorized to conduct such inspections. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95, § 18; Ord. of 9-10-96) 
Sec. 6-39. - Gambling on premises prohibited. 
There shall be no gambling, betting, games of chance, punch-board, slot machines, pin-ball machines, or the operation of any scheme for hazarding money or any other thing of value in any place of business licensed under this article, or in any room adjoining the same, owned, leased or controlled by a licensee. Any violation of this section shall be cause for suspension or revocation of a license. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95, § 19) 
Sec. 6-40. - Grounds for suspension or revocation of license. 
Any of the following shall be grounds for suspension or revocation, as the governing authority sees fit, of a license: 
(a)  The making of any statement on an application for a license issued hereunder which shall be later found to be false; 
(b)  Violation of any of the terms of this article; 
(c)  With respect to the licensee or any person with an ownership interest in the licensed premises, the violation of any federal, state or local law relating to the sale, control or regulation of alcoholic beverages, drugs, gambling, or taxation. 
(d)  Failure to maintain adequate financial responsibility upon which issuance of the license was conditioned, or default on any obligation, of any kind whatsoever, lawfully owing to Peach County, Georgia; 
(e)  Suspension or revocation of a state retail dealer's license, which shall automatically operate to suspend or revoke any license issued hereunder. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95, § 20; Ord. of 9-10-96) 
Sec. 6-40.1. - Suspension and revocation—Procedure; hearing. 
Any action taken by the governing authority to suspend or revoke a license issued hereunder shall not preclude and may be in addition to any criminal prosecution by a proper authority as provided by the laws and ordinances of Peach County, the State of Georgia, or the United States. Whenever any action is taken by the governing authority to suspend or revoke any license issued hereunder, the governing authority shall provide written notice to the licensee within 10 days of such action, said notice stating the action taken and the reasons therefor. The licensee shall have 15 days following notification of such action to request a hearing before the governing authority, which hearing shall be held within 30 days of such request. The licensee shall be entitled at such hearing to present evidence and to examine opposing witnesses either with or without counsel. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95, § 20; Ord. of 9-10-96) 
Sec. 6-41. - Repeal of conflicting ordinances. 
All ordinances and parts of ordinances in conflict herewith are hereby expressly repealed. 
(Ord. of 9-12-95, § 21) 
Sec. 6-42. - Multiple locations; separate license required. 
Each license issued hereunder shall authorize the sale of malt beverages or wine at one licensed premises only. A person selling alcoholic beverages at more than one licensed premises must obtain a separate license for each location. 
(Ord. of 9-10-96; Mo. of 11-6-96) 
Sec. 6-43. - Operation in accordance with law. 
Licensees shall operate in accordance with the terms of this article and with all applicable federal and state law related to the regulation of alcoholic beverages, including but not limited to the Georgia Alcoholic Beverage Code, O.C.G.A. 3-3-1 et seq. The term "licensee" as used in this part includes agents and employees of the licensee. 
(Ord. of 9-10-96) 
Sec. 6-44. - License issuance; application procedure. 
(a)  Application. Application for a retail dealer's license shall be made on forms furnished by the governing authority. Applications shall be made in the name of a natural person and shall include the name of the business entity which will operate pursuant to the license, and the names of all individuals holding an ownership interest in the business entity. 
(b)  Fee. The fee for each retail dealer's license shall be as established by the county commission per annum and shall be paid prior to the issuance of such license, said fee to accompany the application, and shall be either a bank certified check or money order. 
(c)  Background investigation. Each applicant shall furnish a complete set of fingerprints which shall be forwarded to the Peach County Sheriff's Department who shall search the files of the Georgia Crime Information Center for a period of two years immediately preceding the date of such application for any instance of criminal activity. The Peach County Sheriff's Department shall also submit such fingerprints to the Federal Bureau of Investigation under rules established by the United States Department of Justice for processing and identification records. The Federal record, if any, shall be obtained and returned to the governing authority considering such application. When considering an application for renewal of a license, the governing authority may waive compliance with all or any part of this paragraph. 
(Ord. of 9-10-96; Ord. of 8-12-14) 
Sec. 6-45. - Same—Standards for granting and renewing licenses. 
(a)  Financial responsibility. All applicants for a retail dealer's license must show financial responsibility. The governing authority may require all applicants to provide financial statements and other evidence of financial responsibility in conjunction with the application. An application may be denied to any applicant where it appears that the applicant would not have adequate financial resources to direct and manage the affairs of the business. 
(b)  Legal age. The applicant must be at least 21 years of age. 
(c)  County employees ineligible. No employee of Peach County, Georgia shall be eligible to receive a retail dealer's license. 
(d)  Violation of laws. No retail dealer's license shall be granted or renewed where the individual applicant, or any individual with an ownership interest in the business entity which will operate pursuant to the license, has been convicted of, or has entered a plea of guilty or nolo contendere to, any crime related to the sale or regulation of alcoholic beverages, gambling, drugs, or tax law violations, within the two-year period preceding the application date. This section shall not apply to a person who has previously had his or her license revoked by the governing authority. 
(e)  Prior revocation. No person whose retail dealer's license has been revoked by the governing authority shall be granted a license for a period of 12 months from the date the revocation becomes final, or for such lesser period as the governing authority may determine in its discretion, except that no person whose license is revoked by the governing authority due to conviction of, or a plea of guilty or nolo contendere to, a crime related to drugs, gambling, or tax law violations shall be granted a license for a period of two; years from the date the revocation becomes final. No business in which any such person has an ownership interest shall be entitled to operate pursuant to a license for 12 months following the revocation of such person's license. A license revocation becomes final (1) upon the expiration of any applicable period, as provided by this Ordinance or as allowed by law, to request a hearing or appeal with regard to the revocation decision, if no hearing or appeal is requested; or (2) by a decision of the Superior Court of Peach County which has the effect of affirming a decision of the governing authority revoking a license. 
(f)  Condition of premises. No retail dealer's license shall be issued to any person unless the building in which the business will be located is complete and detailed plans of said building and outside premises are attached to the application, or unless proposed plans and specifications and a building permit for a building to be built or renovated are attached to the application. The completed building or the proposed building shall comply with ordinances of Peach County, Georgia, regulations of the State Revenue Commissioner and the laws of the State of Georgia. The proposed building shall also be subject to final inspection and approval when completed by the Building Inspector for Peach County. Each such building shall contain sufficient lighting so that the building itself and the premises on all sides of the building are readily visible at all times from the street on which the building is located so as to reveal the inside retail area of the building and so as to reveal all of the outside premises of said building. Each applicant for a retail dealer's license shall attach to his application evidence of ownership of the building or proposed building or a copy of the lease if the applicant is leasing the building. A separate retail dealer's license shall be required for each place of business. 
(g)  Location. No retail dealer's license shall be granted to any person unless the entire business premises of the proposed location, including parking lot, is situated not less than 100 yards from any church building, not less than 200 yards from the property line of any school ground or college campus, not less than 100 yards from any building used as an alcohol rehabilitation center, and not less than 1,000 feet from any licenced adult entertainment establishment. Distance shall be measured by the most direct route of travel on the ground. Each application for a retail dealer's license shall include a scale drawing of the location of the proposed premises showing the distance to the nearest church building, school ground or campus, alcohol rehabilitation center, or adult entertainment establishment, or a certificate of a registered surveyor that such location complies with this ordinance with reference to this section. 
(Ord. of 9-10-96) 
Sec. 6-46. - Same—Temporary issuance. 
Where it appears to the governing authority that an application is complete except for the F.B.I. report as described in paragraph 6-44(c) above, and that the applicant otherwise qualifies for a retail dealer's licence, the governing authority may grant the license contingent on receiving a satisfactory F.B.I. report. Should the report provide grounds for denying the license, the license may be revoked immediately as though the application had been denied, and the licensee shall have the right to a hearing as provided in section 6-23. 
(Ord. of 9-10-96) 
Sec. 6-47. - Same—Denial; hearing. 
All decisions of the governing authority either approving or denying a license application shall be stated in writing and a copy of such statement shall be provided to the applicant either personally or by certified mail within ten days of the decision. Whenever the governing authority shall deny an application for a retail dealer's license, the applicant shall have fifteen days following notification of denial to request a hearing before the governing authority. The applicant shall be entitled to present evidence and cross-examine opposing witnesses at such hearing either with or without legal counsel. 
(Ord. of 9-10-96) 
Secs. 6-48, 6-49. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - RETAIL SALES OF DISTILLED SPIRITS FOR CONSUMPTION ON THE PREMISES 

Sec. 6-50. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Alcohol means ethyl alcohol, hydrated oxide of ethyl or spirits of wine, from whatever source or by whatever process produced. 
Alcoholic beverage means and includes all alcohol, distilled spirits, beer, malt, beverage, wine or fortified wine. 
Distilled spirits means any alcoholic beverage obtained by distillation or containing more than 21 percent alcohol by volume, including, but not limited to, all fortified wines. 
Fortified wine means any alcoholic beverage containing more than 21 percent alcohol by volume made from fruits, berries or grapes either by natural fermentation or by natural fermentation with brandy added. The term includes, but is not limited to, brandy. 
Governing authority means the Board of Commissioners of Peach County. 
Licensee means the person whose name appears upon a retail dealer's license and shall include the business entity operating pursuant under one name. 
Licensed premises means the business location of a licensed retail dealer existing on a single contiguous tract of real estate and operating under one name. 
Package means a bottle, can, keg, barrel, or other original consumer container. 
Person means any individual, firm, partnership, cooperative, non-profit membership corporation, joint venture, association, company, corporation, agency syndicate, estate, trust, business trust, receiver, fiduciary, or other group or combination acting as a unit, body politic, or political subdivision, whether public, private or quasi- public. 
Retail dealer means any person who sells distilled spirits for consumption on the premises, at retail only to consumers and not for resale. 
Retail dealer's license or license means a license to sell distilled spirits at retail for consumption on the premises, issued by the governing authority pursuant to and subject to the terms of this article. 
Wine means any alcoholic beverage containing not more than 21 percent alcohol by volume made from fruits, berries or grapes either by natural fermentation or by natural fermentation with brandy added. The term includes, but is not limited to, all sparkling wines, wines and like products. The term does not include cooking wine mixed with salt or other ingredients so as to render it unfit for human consumption as a beverage. A liquid shall first be deemed to be a wine at that point in the manufacturing process when it conforms to the definition of wine contained in this section. 
(Ord. of 5-8-2012) 
Sec. 6-51. - Familiarity with article. 
It shall be the duty of each licensee to maintain a copy of this article on the premises, and to instruct each employee as to the terms thereof; and each licensee and employee shall at all times be familiar with this article. 
(Ord. of 5-8-2012) 
Sec. 6-52. - Responsibility for acts of employees and others. 
Licensees are charged with the responsibility hereunder for compliance with this article by their officers, agents, servants and employees. 
(Ord. of 5-8-2012) 
Sec. 6-53. - Removal of alcoholic beverage served for consumption on the promises prohibited. 
No alcoholic beverage sold pursuant to a license for sales of distilled spirits for consumption on the premises may be removed from the premises on which such alcoholic beverage is sold. 
(Ord. of 5-8-2012) 
Sec. 6-54. - Construction of definitions. 
As used in this article, defined words shall have the meanings specified unless the context in which the word or term is used clearly requires that a different meaning be used. 
(Ord. of 5-8-2012) 
Sec. 6-55. - Retail dealer licenses; applications; notice; fingerprints; bonds; restrictions; standards; hearing. 
(a)  No distilled spirits for consumption on the premises shall be sold in Peach County except as authorized by a retail dealer's license issued pursuant to this article. Licenses issued hereunder shall authorize the sale of distilled spirits for consumption on the premises as defined herein, only. 
(b)  Application for a retail dealer's license shall be made on forms furnished by the governing authority. A notice of each application shall be advertised in the official gazette of Peach County, Georgia once a week for two weeks immediately preceding the meeting of the governing authority in which the application is to be acted upon. 
(c)  Each applicant shall furnish a complete set of fingerprints which shall be forwarded to the Peach County Sheriff's Department who shall search the files of the Georgia Crime Information Center for a period of five years immediately preceding the date of such application for any instance of criminal activity. The Peach County Sheriff's Department shall also submit such fingerprints to the Federal Bureau of Investigation under rules established by the United States Department of Justice for processing and identification records. The federal record, if any, shall be obtained and returned to the governing authority considering such application. Where it appears to the governing authority that an application is complete except for the F.B.I. fingerprint report, and that the applicant otherwise qualifies for a retail dealer's license, the governing authority may grant the license contingent on receiving a satisfactory F.B.I. report. Should the report provide grounds for denying the license, the license may be revoked immediately as though the application had been denied, and the licensee shall have the right to a hearing. 
(d)  Along with their application, applicants must post with the governing authority a personal performance bond, said bond to be conditioned upon the faithful observance and performance by the licensee of the rules and regulations contained in this article. Upon the violation of this article, or any part thereof, the amount of the bond to be forfeited will be determined by the governing authority in accordance with the nature of the violation after a hearing is held by the said governing authority. Written notice of such hearing shall be given to the alleged violator not less than 15 days prior thereto. The determination by the governing authority to forfeit such bond may be in addition to an action taken by the governing authority under sections 6-72 through 6-72.1. Said bond shall be payable to Peach County, Georgia in the amount of $1,000.00, said bond to be approved by the governing authority and shall be executed in the form specified by the governing authority.
